Achievements of League of Nations Sanctions: Italian Trade Decreases by One-Third, Britain Suffers the Greatest Sacrifice 45

(Geneva) According to the first official report on the impact of the League of Nations sanctions against Italy, Italy and its colonies' trade with the 47 countries implementing sanctions has decreased by one-third. This total was compiled by the League of Nations Economic Intelligence Service at the request of the Committee of Eighteen. It is limited to the achievements of the first four months of the implementation of sanctions. It states that Italian exports have decreased from US$68 million to US$45 million, and imports have decreased from US$73 million to US$64 million. In addition, Italy has lost US$63 million in gold reserves. These figures show that Britain has made the greatest sacrifice among the League of Nations countries in fulfilling its obligations. On average, the League of Nations countries have lost 44% of their export trade to Italy due to fulfilling their covenant, while Britain alone has lost 92%. In February 1935, Britain shipped goods to Italy worth US$18,417,000, while only US$82,100 was shipped last month. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

(Geneva) The Chairman of the Economic Sanctions Committee today distributed a 15-page memorandum to the member states of the League of Nations, detailing the impact of economic sanctions on trade. The statistics, from November of last year to January of this year, are all based on the gold standard. This official document was published one day before the meeting of the Committee of Thirteen, and its meaning is even more important. The Chairman of the Economic Sanctions Committee stated in the attached letter that if necessary, the Committee of Eighteen will be convened for a meeting as soon as possible to discuss.

The memorandum pointed out that Italian exports to Britain, since the implementation of sanctions (November 1935 to January 1936), have decreased from US$2,800,000 to US$700,000; exports to France have decreased from US$2,200,000 to US$160,000; exports to the United States have decreased from US$3,500,000 to US$1,900,000; and exports to the Netherlands have decreased from US$180,000 to US$77,000. However, exports to Germany, Austria, and Hungary have remained almost the same. Imports have also decreased at the same time. Imports from Britain have decreased from US$850,000 to US$150,000; imports from France have decreased from US$2,900,000 to US$700,000; and imports from the United States have decreased from US$5,500,000 to US$700,000. France and Sweden are more important for gold imports. (National Telegram, 15th)

The Food of Peking Man at Zhoukoudian (Part 1) 50

— Originally written by Dr. Ralph W. Chaney, Translated by Chen Shaoyan

We can only guess at the eating habits of the earliest primitive humans. A million years ago, our human ancestors had not yet learned the art of writing, so they left behind no lists of foods or books on cooking methods that could serve as evidence of their food choices.

We can speculate, based on the diets of modern great apes, that they consumed both plants and animals. This omnivorous diet is also suggested by the nature of the fossil teeth of early humans. These teeth seem suitable for chewing a wide variety of foods, including both meat and plants.

In the early written records of humans, until recently, no concrete evidence about their food can be found. The Java Erect Ape-man (Pithecanthropus erectus) was not discovered until 1891, but all that could be represented were only a part of the skull and a few remaining bones. The historical material represented by the Early Man or Ancient Ape-man (Eoanthropus, Pildown) of Piltdown in England is also incomplete. Apart from the material provided by his teeth, no one has ever raised questions or discussions about food and eating habits.

This problem was not solved until the discovery of the third type of proto-human. This type of proto-human, like the aforementioned Erect Ape-man and Early Man, lived far back in the early Ice Age. In this way, it can also be said that the actual dwelling place of our earliest ancestors was discovered.

Members of the Geological Survey of China, under the guidance of Dr. Davidson Black, have excavated numerous skulls and teeth of the oldest proto-humans living in Asia over the past six years. Also excavated in the old home of these ancient cave dwellers were many stone tools, hearth bottoms, and uneaten food scraps. This can be regarded as the first record of the food of the oldest known humans in Asia.

Millions of years ago, many limestones were deposited and accumulated in shallow seas, and are now exposed in the Western Hills near the ancient capital of Beijing, China. Due to the dissolving power of underground springs, the mountains have been pierced into many caves, which have been used as dwellings by ancient Chinese proto-humans, and as underground nests by hyenas and other beasts. Some of the caves have been blocked because fragments of rock have fallen from the top and walls of the caves from time to time. These fallen fragments have gradually cemented into hard masses, commonly known as breccia, after being deposited by water containing limestone.

As time slowly passed, and it came to our time, Chinese workers came to the mountains to mine limestone. They were preparing to use these stone materials as building materials or as the foundation stones of roads. They encountered these irregular, angular breccia blocks, which had not been touched because of their impure texture. In 1923, the prestigious Swedish paleontologist J.G. Anderson studied these breccia blocks and discovered many fossil skeletons of extinct rhinoceroses, wild buffaloes, and other beasts in northern China. Through such hard excavation work, the oldest history of Asian humans was uncovered from these breccia blocks containing fossil skeletons!

Zhoukoudian Town, located thirty miles west of Peiping (Beijing), is a center for inland coal mining and limestone extraction. A railway was built there several years ago to transport those heavy products to Peiping, but due to the political instability in northern China in recent years, the vehicles used for transportation are sometimes used for war activities. As a result, long camel caravans, all Bactrian camels from inland Asia, appeared on this dusty road with heavy steps, and donkeys, often wasting time, trudged up the long slopes to the mines.

On the small hill above Zhoukoudian, near the cave, where the most ossified fossils are accumulated, the Geological Survey of China has built a very comfortable laboratory and residences for the scientific workers engaged in the excavation. There are often visitors from all over the world, including many famous anthropologists and paleontologists, to see the most complete record of these earliest humans. The hillside is covered with fragments of breccia removed from the cave, and the entrance to the cave is covered with rock to avoid the strong sunlight.

This seems to be true: in the past, there were one or more entrances and exits here, which were used as doorways by proto-humans or beasts. These cave entrances have probably collapsed and been blocked, so they may discover more important facts that are unknown now during future excavations. Going down from the limestone passages to a depth of sixty feet from the current entrance and exit, the bottom layer of the cave is reached, which is the real residence of the oldest residents of Asia! Here, it has been covered by many feet of breccia, and many skulls have been recorded. From these skulls, we know that the wisdom of these human ancestors has reached above the level of the beasts.

The Cave where the "Peking Man" Skull was Discovered in Zhoukoudian

(Special dispatch on the 16th)

(Nanjing) The second annual meeting of the first Council of Academia Sinica was held at the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica at 9 a.m. on the 16th. A total of thirteen proposals were submitted to four groups for review and then submitted to the afternoon general assembly for discussion. As a result, they were all revised and passed separately. (Central News Agency telegram on the 16th)

Resolutions of the Annual Meeting 52

(Nanjing) The first annual meeting of the Council of Academia Sinica was held on the 16th. As a result of the discussion of the proposals, the proposal by President Cai on the outline of the working policy of the Academia Sinica was resolved and passed. The case that Chinese scientific research should pay special attention to the urgent needs of the country, society, and practical method was discussed, and it was requested that the Academia Sinica negotiate with domestic research institutions to actively focus on scientific research related to national defense and production. It was resolved that A. Research work should pay special attention to the urgent needs of the country and society, including all types of science. B. The Academia Sinica should inform all its affiliated research institutes and other important academic institutions in the country to adopt this idea in the allocation of funds. C. The Council of Academia Sinica should, within the scope of each discipline, specifically list the problems that the country and society most urgently need to solve, estimating that considerable results can be achieved in two or three years, and send them to the Academia Sinica, which will then distribute them to relevant academic institutions for work. D. If government agencies have any problems that need to be researched, they can consult with the Academia Sinica on how to proceed. E. Academic institutions should report the research methods and results obtained on the above problems to the Council of Academia Sinica at any time. The proposal that the Council of Academia Sinica should make efforts to promote cooperation in domestic and foreign scientific work was resolved. A. The principle was approved. B. Preliminary review method: The council will send a letter to the embassies abroad and the student supervisors, stating that the names, subjects, and thesis titles of students who have graduated from foreign countries should be sent to the council annually, and it would be even better if the thesis could be attached. The council will send a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Education, stating that all international conferences related to academic research should be notified to the council so that it can provide the government with opinions on whether China should participate in the conference. C. The council will send a letter to domestic academic institutions and organizations, stating that all information about their participation in international academic work should be reported to the council. D. Please ask the Academia Sinica to investigate and collect the organization history and past conference overviews of important international academic conferences as much as possible for reference. C. Advanced methods: Please ask the Academia Sinica to consult with the Ministry of Education to evaluate. The proposal to consult with various research institutions to open up research rooms and libraries to encourage scientific research was resolved. The proposal stated that the academy and most domestic research institutions have already implemented all points within a possible range, so there seems to be no need to discuss it again. The proposal that the Academia Sinica's Institutes of Physics, Chemistry, and Engineering should jointly organize a scientific instrument manufacturing institute with the government or large businesses was resolved. There are many types of scientific instruments, and the country's technical talents are not enough to meet the needs. The construction of large-scale instrument factories is not easy to achieve at once. The academy seems to be able only to follow its established policy, encourage domestic businesses that can manufacture various instruments themselves, and provide technical assistance. The proposal that the Council of Academia Sinica should appropriately commend those who have made outstanding achievements in scientific research in the country was resolved and passed. The proposal to add international scientific research conferences to the council was resolved. The Academia Sinica will decide on the participation methods and submit them to the government for resolution. Please ask the Academia Sinica to consult with the Ministry of Education on how to handle it. The proposal to plan the source of membership fees for my country to join the International Astronomical Society was resolved. The participating groups can be organized by the Chinese Astronomical Society and the Astronomical Research Institute. The required funds can be discussed and assisted by the Academia Sinica and the Ministry of Education. The draft articles of association for the Yang Quan Ding Wenjiang Scholarship was resolved and the principle was passed. The detailed methods will be determined by the Central Research Army. The proposal to compile a catalog of specialized works from various groups was resolved and passed according to the principles determined by the review. The specialized catalogs compiled in the future should be printed and distributed in groups. Also, Wang Shijie temporarily proposed to amend Article 12 of the Council's election regulations as follows: Candidates for council members will be elected by a roll-call voting method, and the final election will be by a secret ballot voting method. It was resolved and passed. It was also decided that the next annual meeting of the Council will be held during the spring vacation next year. The date will be decided by the secretary. (Central News Agency telegram on the 16th)

Details of the Rome Conference of Italy, Austria, and Hungary 89

— Correspondence from Rome

Two years ago, Italy, Austria, and Hungary signed the "Rome Accords," forming a bloc through economic reciprocity and cultural cooperation. When the League of Nations discussed economic sanctions against Italy, the representatives of Austria and Hungary stated they could not participate, precisely because of this bloc relationship, which prevented them from joining in an unfriendly action towards Italy. Recently, Germany reoccupied the Rhineland with great force, which even France could not deter. Austria was concerned about the stability of its independent status. Italy, with its victories in the war against Abyssinia, was seeking to restore its dominance in Central Europe. Therefore, on the second anniversary of the Rome Accords, it convened Austria and Hungary in Rome for a meeting, hence the origin of this conference.

Participants: The delegations from Austria and Hungary arrived in Rome at 6 p.m. on March 20th. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini personally welcomed them at the station. The Austrian delegation included Chancellor Schuschnigg, Foreign Minister Guido Schmidt, Director of International Politics at the State Council Hornbostel, and the personal secretaries of Schuschnigg and Schmidt. The Hungarian delegation included Prime Minister Gömbös, Foreign Minister Kánya, Director of the State Council's Information Bureau Mikecz, Director of the Foreign Ministry's Information Bureau Mender, and the personal secretaries of Gömbös and Kánya. The Italian ambassadors to Austria, Plessi, and to Hungary, Clonar, also accompanied the delegations to Italy.

Public Agreements: After arriving in Rome, the delegations attended banquets, watched a play at the Royal Theater, visited the Royal University of Rome, and reviewed a cavalry school drill. They held two meetings with the Italian side at the Palazzo Venezia. The Italian attendees included Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Mussolini, Undersecretary for Foreign Affairs Suvich, and Director-General of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Aloisi. The conference was divided into secret and public parts. The public part resulted in the establishment of "Supplementary Rome Accords," officially signed on March 23rd, consisting of three items, as follows:

The Prime Ministers of Italy, Austria, and Hungary, meeting again in Rome on March 21, 1936, expressed great satisfaction with the continued cooperation between the three countries for the purpose of European peace and economic prosperity. Therefore, they solemnly decided to continue the spirit of the Rome Accords of March 17, 1934, trusting and collaborating in political, economic, and cultural matters. At the same time, in order to develop the interests of the three countries in any aspect and to address the European situation, they decided to form a bloc and establish a permanent mechanism for consultation.

To comply with the aforementioned purpose, the three countries decided that in the future, no major political issues concerning the Danube River would be discussed or agreed upon by any one of the three countries without the consent of the other two. However, any economic agreements already concluded between the three countries and other Danube-related countries would not be bound by this restriction.

The aforementioned permanent consultation mechanism will be composed of the foreign ministers of the three countries. Meetings will be held both regularly and irregularly. The dates of the former will be determined separately, while the latter will be convened when the three governments deem it necessary. The present document will be in Italian, German, and Hungarian. In case of linguistic disputes, the Italian version will be used as the standard for resolution.

Secret Deliberations: In addition to the public agreements, the conference also involved secret deliberations, which had been discussed prior to the meeting. The son of Austrian Vice-Chancellor Starhemberg came to Rome on March 4th to introduce Schuschnigg, and the ambassadors of the three countries had also held secret discussions. These discussions were further confirmed at the conference. According to reporters, the main contents of these secret deliberations included four items:

Absolute guarantee of Austria's sovereignty, independence, and territorial integrity to maintain security in Central Europe.

Establishment of a military alliance between the three countries.

Economic and financial alliance between the three countries.

Efforts to conclude a Central European pact led by the three countries. In addition, it was decided that the various agreements reached at this conference would be tentatively set for a term of three years, after which further consultations would be held depending on the development of the European situation. The permanent consultation mechanism between the three countries would also meet at any time to seek close cooperation between the three countries.

Prospects for Central European Politics: The relations between Italy, Austria, and Hungary have been exceptionally close since the conclusion of the 1934 Accords. Italy has granted special tariff treatment to Austrian industrial exports and Hungarian grain exports. At the same time, Austria and Hungary have also extended preferential treatment to Italian goods. Italy has also donated a large number of aircraft, and there has been extensive cultural cooperation between the three countries. For example, a large number of Austrian and Hungarian students came to Italy last year to study. The Perugian International University has established a Hungarian section in addition to the English, German, and French sections, with more than 100 Hungarian students studying there. After the Rome conference, the three countries secretly formed a military alliance. This can protect Austria's independence, and Italy's position as a Central European leader will be strengthened, increasing its influence in discussions with Britain and France. In order to oppose Germany, France has recently openly demanded the abolition of economic sanctions against Italy, making its desire for reconciliation with Italy very clear. However, how Italy will use this superior diplomatic position and what developments will occur in Central European politics after this Rome conference are matters worthy of attention. (Sent by Xu Xingchu from Rome on the evening of March 25th)

Major Fire in Huangsha, Guangzhou, on Tiyun Road 90

Eighty to Ninety Shops Were Burned Down, More Than One Hundred People Were Injured, and Losses Exceeded One Million Dollars

Guangzhou Correspondence: Huangsha in Guangzhou is a prosperous area west of the city, facing the Pearl River to the south, with numerous sails and masts. At its western end is the Huangsha Main Station, the terminal of the southern section of the Yuehan Railway, connecting the North River and reaching Wuhan. Travelers and merchants come and go frequently. Several years ago, due to the lack of roads, it suffered a major fire. After the fire, roads were built, the city appearance was renewed, and transportation became more convenient than before. Unexpectedly, at around 1 a.m. on the 11th of this month, a major fire broke out again in the area of Tiyun West Road, Conggui Road, and Mibu Street, burning down eighty to ninety shops, injuring over one hundred firefighters and rescuers, and spreading to the warehouse of the Explosives Monopoly Bureau. The hazardous materials stored there, such as white powder and silver powder, numbered in the thousands of boxes, all consumed by the flames. Consequently, the raging flames soared into the sky, and explosive debris flew in all directions, causing harm to nearby residents and firefighters. Firefighting was particularly difficult. The details are recorded below:

Tragic Scene of the Burning: At around 1 a.m. on the 11th, while the city residents were sound asleep, a fire suddenly broke out in the rear of the Shenghe Warehouse at No. 3, First Lane, Conggui Road, and the western part of the rear of the Di Ji Peanut Shop at No. 25, Tiyun Road. The flames lit up the sky. By the time the shop employees realized it and sounded the alarm, the fire had already spread. Moreover, the north wind was very strong that night, causing the fire to spread even faster. In an instant, the fire had spread to four locations. Burning south, the back of the rice shops on Mibu Street and the Anle Soda Factory were burned simultaneously. Shops on Tiyun West Road and Desheng Lane on the left and right also suddenly caught fire. Soon, the warehouse of the Explosives Monopoly Bureau at No. 19, First Lane, Conggui Road, containing 1,700 barrels of white powder and explosive leaves, was heated and exploded. At that moment, the fire scene resembled a battlefield, with flames shooting in all directions and white light filling the sky. During the explosions, the ground shook, and door plaques fell one after another. Bricks and tiles flew in all directions. Refugees in the disaster area were scorched and disheveled. Firefighters retreated uniformly. Some who could not escape in time were burned by the fire, reaching over thirty people. The fire engine of the Huangsha Fire Substation was partially destroyed because it was close to the fire scene. The other fire engines of the Fire Department, including Nos. 11, 13, 6, 2, 4, and 8, drew water from the east, west, north, and south and sprayed from afar. The Jinghua Fire Ship, facing the Pearl River, drew water from the river surface and used hoses for remote firefighting. The firefighters bravely dismantled the fire pits and rescued refugees trapped in the fire scene. At that time, cries of distress filled the air, mixed with the sound of explosions, and the collapse of buildings. Displaced refugees huddled on the Shaji Road and Conggui Road. Some lost their children, some abandoned the elderly and weak, and some were groaning in pain. Various charitable organizations immediately dispatched teams to rescue the injured and engage in rescue work.

Number of Deaths and Injuries: That night, the injured firefighters included Zeng Shaoxiong, Chen Xia, Chen Yuan, Liu Rong, and Liu Xiwu, totaling thirty-two. Injured residents included Chen Wenan, Liu Hongqing, Luo Guangming, Lu Bin, Zong Wen, Wang Mingan, Li Chi, Chen Zucheng, Liang Song, Chen Youzhu, Zhou Ji, Dong Liu, Tan Sen, Fan Luoming, Wu Xing, Liang Shugui, Lu Jieping, Lu Sumei, Chen Nv, Li Yongsen, Chen Bing, Liu Rixiu, Mrs. Li, He Baishan, Zou Weichao, Zou Yuebang, Guan Ziying, Lin Jiebiao, Song Meijiao, totaling over thirty people. According to firefighters at the scene, more than ten people were burned to death due to being unable to escape. Due to the traffic disruption, the bodies were not exhumed until the next day. In addition, there were forty to fifty injured people who were not registered, bringing the total number of severely injured to over one hundred and twenty.

Shops Burned Down: Starting from No. 3, First Lane, Conggui Road, about thirty shops were burned down. The back of the rice shops on Mibu Street was completely destroyed by the fire. More than twenty households were burned in Desheng Lane. Shops burned on Tiyun West Road included Da Ji Shop at No. 1, Yun Yuan Tea House at No. 3, vacant shops at Nos. 4 and 7, Xie Fa Iron Shop at No. 9, Jiang Guilin Shop at No. 17, Chang Sheng Shop at No. 19, Yu Long Shop at No. 21, Zhong He Shop at No. 23, Di Ji Shop at No. 25, Fu Sheng Ju at No. 27, You Sheng Shop at No. 29, Huo Hou He Tang Charity Clinic at No. 31, Shun Tai Shop at No. 39, Xin Feng Shop at No. 41, Bi Residence at No. 1, Shende Water Lane, Deng Residence at No. 11, Desheng Lane, Zheng Residence at No. 13, Liang Residence at No. 15, Yang Residence at No. 19, Li Residence at No. 32, Wu Residence at No. 34, Lu Residence at No. 36, Luo Residence at No. 38, Luo Residence at No. 40, Zeng Residence at No. 41, Si He Shop at No. 41, Liang Residence at No. 1, West Fort Ditch, Li Residence at No. 2, Fan Residence at No. 4, Huang Residence at No. 3, Nan He Shop at No. 38, Yi Mei Street, toilet at No. 40, Nan He Warehouse at No. 42, Nos. 1, 3, 5, 7, 9, 11, 13, and 15, First Lane, Conggui Road, all vacant shops, Tong Zhi Machine Shop at No. 17, warehouse at No. 19, vacant shops at Nos. 11 and 13, Mibu Street, Zhong Hua Shop at No. 29, Shen Long Shop at No. 3, Zhong Hua Shop warehouses at Nos. 36 and 38, He Li Rice Milling Shop at No. 42, Shen Long Shop at No. 40, He He Rice Shop at No. 44, half of Anle Soda Factory was burned, Tong He Shop at No. 41, Yu Hua Shop at No. 24, both had their rear sections burned, the front section of No. 18 was burned, Gong Xing Warehouse at No. 34, Yu Chang Rice Shop at No. 28, vacant shops at Nos. 26 and 20, a packing shop at No. 12, and three boats near Liu Bo Ditch were also burned. Based on what is known, a total of over eighty shops were burned.

Estimated Losses: Excluding the goods, the value of the burned shops alone is estimated to be no less than 500,000 yuan. The largest loss was the 1,700 boxes of white powder and 50 boxes of silver powder stored in the warehouse of the Explosives Monopoly Bureau, each box weighing 84 catties and 100 catties respectively, with a total value of over 190,000 yuan. The losses of goods and residences in other shops have not yet been fully calculated.

Aftermath: The great fire took until 3 p.m. on the 11th to be completely extinguished. At 11 a.m., the embers of the burlap shop on Mibu Street reignited. Residents, thinking that another fire was about to break out, urgently requested assistance. The Fire Department dispatched two more fire engines to the scene to extinguish the flames. The embers were finally extinguished in the afternoon. Afterwards, the police investigated the cause of the fire and detained Pan, the manager of Shenghe Shop at No. 3, First Lane, Conggui Road, and He, the owner of Di Ji Shop, for questioning at the Huangsha Branch Bureau. Both Pan and He denied that the fire started in their shops, but the residents strongly accused them. The Branch Chief, considering the seriousness of the matter, kept the two in custody pending further investigation. (April 11th evening)

Martial Law Declared in Quanzhou, Fujian 91

Due to Treacherous Collaborators Secretly Plotting Disruption, Seven Regulations for Martial Law are Stipulated

Xiamen Correspondence: Recently, there have been reports of instability in southern Fujian, with Quanzhou and Yongchun as the central areas, followed by Zhangzhou. The Pacification Commissioner's Office and the Third Pacification Area Command stationed in Quanzhou have issued orders to all subordinate garrisons to strictly guard against any disturbances. The Quanzhou Pacification Command has been particularly strict in its deployment and search of the defense areas under its jurisdiction. The headquarters of the 52nd Regiment of the 9th Division stationed in Quanzhou City announced a temporary martial law order for Quanzhou City and important towns under its jurisdiction from the night of April 9th, and the proclamation of martial law is as follows: "Proclamation: According to reports, many bandits, traitors, and vagrants have infiltrated various important towns in Jinjiang, secretly plotting disruption, and some are posing as refugees, inquiring about local conditions everywhere, showing obvious reactionary behavior. If they are not strictly arrested, it will be insufficient to maintain security. The following regulations are hereby stipulated, and all Lianbao chiefs and Baojia chiefs must strictly comply. Violators will be subject to joint liability. 1. From this (9th) day, temporary martial law is declared in various important towns under Quanzhou jurisdiction. From 11 p.m. to 5 a.m. the following morning, people are not allowed to enter or exit. Military and government personnel are not allowed to pass through the sentry line without official business. 2. All hotels, inns, hospitals, and public institutions that accommodate guests must report to this headquarters for record-keeping and must not conceal them. 3. All Baojia chiefs and militia teams must mobilize in full force to assist the military and police in arresting suspicious persons. 4. The troops stationed at each city gate must strictly check the people entering and exiting. If there are any suspicious persons, they must be arrested immediately. 5. Patrol teams should increase patrols. If they encounter suspicious persons, they must immediately interrogate or arrest them. 6. When the people are interrogated by the military, they should clearly state which Baojia they belong to. If they are from out of town, they should state their business, where they come from, and who they know in Quanzhou. 7. Refugees are not allowed to reside in public places, temples, ancestral halls, etc. in each Bao. The above seven items are hereby proclaimed for immediate knowledge and compliance by all parties."

Quanzhou Prefecture includes the five counties of Jinjiang, Nan'an, Hui'an, Tong'an, and Anxi. Jinjiang, Nan'an, Hui'an, and Tong'an are all coastal counties, which are important areas in southern Fujian, on the west coast of the Taiwan Strait. Furthermore, the Security Office recently captured Liao Heqin, an important member of a secret organization in southern Fujian. According to his confession, his accomplices include Chen Wei-yuan, He Xianzu, Yang Hanlie, Lin Daokuan, Hong Zheming, Guo Zong, Guo Lougu, Wu Peng, Li Fa, Yang Qiyuan, Zhang Jingshan, Li Jinri, He Lifu, Zhang Xiling, and Huang Ada, totaling fifteen people. On the 10th, the Security Office presented a report to the province requesting that these fifteen people be declared wanted for endangering the Republic of China. It is found that Chen Wei-yuan is from Minhou and served as a brigade commander in the 19th Route Army in the 17th and 18th years of the Republic. Later, due to a falling out with Chen Mingshu, he came to Fujian to rely on Fang Shengtao and served as the commander of the Second Brigade of the Provincial Defense Army. He resigned after the 19th Route Army entered Fujian. He Xianzu was the former leader of the Putian militia. He was detained when the 19th Route Army entered Fujian and then resigned. Yang Hanlie was the leader of the Anxi militia with a long history. Lin Daokuan was the leader of the Putian militia. Li Fa was the leader of the Hui'an militia. Hong Zheming was the leader of the Tong'an militia. Guo Lougu was the bandit leader of Putian. Guo Zong was the bandit leader of Anxi. However, in southern Fujian, the so-called militia are actually bandits, as they are sometimes incorporated into the army and are therefore called militia. (April 13th)

Strict Tobacco Prohibition in Fujian Province 92

Registration of Smokers Extended and Completed; Those Who Smoke Privately Will Be Executed According to Law

Fuzhou Correspondence: The investigation and prohibition of tobacco planting and the registration of smokers in Fujian Province have been handled very strictly recently. Regarding the prohibition of planting, after Qiu Hongjun was appointed as the special commissioner for investigating and prohibiting tobacco planting in Fujian by the Tobacco Prohibition Commissioner-General, Qiu has arrived in Fujian and has already worked with the Security Office, the Civil Affairs Department, and administrative commissioners of various districts to send commissioners to various counties to conduct on-site inspections to see if farmers have secretly planted tobacco seedlings and whether officials and troops have harbored and levied contributions. So far, nothing has been found. Qiu is now on a tour of inspection to various counties in eastern Fujian and will transfer to southern Fujian in about two weeks. Although the investigation has not yet been completed, the Fujian Provincial Government has been very serious about the prohibition of tobacco planting for the past two years, and it can be predicted that it has reached the stage of thorough elimination. Regarding licensing, the provincial government has already issued an order to the county governments to complete the handling within the extended deadline. If unregistered smokers are found again after the deadline, they will be executed according to law without leniency. The provincial party headquarters also issued an order to the county party headquarters the day before yesterday to assist the local government in handling tobacco prohibition matters and to convene mass organizations to hold expanded tobacco prohibition propaganda to make smokers aware of the alarm and reform themselves. The provincial capital has recently scheduled to hold an expanded anti-drug propaganda week on the 13th of this month. In addition to convening representatives of various agencies and groups to attend the meeting, each Lianbao office should also organize an anti-drug propaganda team to be directed by the county party headquarters to conduct extensive propaganda within the jurisdiction of the Lianbao. At the same time, the Public Security Bureau will commission the household registration officers of each branch bureau to serve concurrently as smoker registration investigators to check whether there are unregistered smokers in their jurisdictions and ask the Baojia chiefs to sign a guarantee stating that there are no unregistered smokers in their jurisdictions. Then, the Baojia chiefs will ask the heads of each household to sign a guarantee stating that there are no private smokers in their household. If unregistered smokers are found in the future, they will all be held jointly liable. The Bao chiefs are now printing admonitions to smoke and registration notices, and affixing them with guarantees, posting them in various households so that everyone knows and fills out the reports. As for the opium paste used by the licensed smokers in this province, it is contracted for transportation and sales by the Tobacco Prohibition Supervision Sub-Office by inviting merchants to divide the districts. The newly appointed Director Cheng Yunshan believes that there are many abuses in the district contracting and has decided to contract the transportation and sales of opium paste throughout the province to only one merchant from the south, with a capital of 600,000 yuan and a pre-payment of a 100,000 yuan deposit. They must sell at least 2,850 dan of Sichuan, Yunnan, Shaanxi, and Gansu opium paste with affixed stamps each year and pay a license fee of 40,000 yuan, allowing them to establish branches and warehouses in Fuzhou and Xiamen to operate wholesale business. Each county will set up only one opium paste shop, which will be contracted separately by the supervision office by inviting merchants, and the amount of opium paste to be sold each year and the amount of license fee to be paid will depend on the size of the county and the amount and grade. (April 15th)

Robbers Killed One Person in Songjiang 93

On the night of the 15th, at about 2 a.m., the home of Shen Zhenqing, a villager in Zhujiahang Township, Punan, was suddenly attacked by more than ten robbers, all speaking in the local dialect. They broke into the house. Shen Zhenqing, hearing the alarm, sneaked out and summoned the guards of the guardhouse and neighbors to gather and arrest the robbers. Shen also joined in the resistance and injured a robber on the spot. The remaining robbers scattered with the stolen goods. The injured robber was then escorted to the Tinglin First Branch Bureau. It was learned that his name was Shen Zirong. Together with the plaintiff, Shen Zhenqing, they hired a boat and escorted him to Songjiang on the same day. While passing near Zhangze, the robber died of exhaustion in the boat. After arriving in Songjiang, the boat berthed at Lishuiguan Bridge and reported to the bureau for inspection. The county's civil servants' labor service has decided to dredge the section from Fangle Bridge to Hezhuang Bridge in the city. Civil servants from various agencies will be assigned to dredge the work. It has been rescheduled to hold a commencement ceremony at the sports ground at 8 a.m. on the 23rd of this month, and the work will be carried out for three days to dredge the section. The corpses at both ends will be dammed on this day.

Baoshan: Xiao Mao's Residence Robbed by Bandits, People Injured 94

At approximately 11 PM the night before last, at Xiao Mao's residence in Wu Jia, Wu Bao, Dacaixiang Township, within the jurisdiction of Baoshan County, a group of fifteen or sixteen bandits suddenly appeared, wearing short shirts and trousers of blue cloth and speaking with local accents. They were armed with iron and wooden clubs, as well as sharp blades, and proceeded to rob the residence. First, they bound and confined all the men, women, old, and young within the house into one room. Then, they arbitrarily searched and looted the premises. During the robbery, Mao Yucai and Mao Peisheng, who cried for help, were slashed in the head by the bandits. The search and robbery lasted for over four hours, until around 4 AM the following morning, when the bandits finally left, fully satisfied with their loot. As they departed, they left behind three iron clubs and a cloth cap. The stolen items are briefly listed as follows: Mao Rulan's family lost 127 yuan in legal tender, 10 silver dollars, a jade ring (worth over ten yuan), a pair of silver bracelets, a silk floss lined jacket, a gold ring, 20,000 copper coins, a pearl powder spoon (with five pearls), and five more pearls. Mao Zonglin's family lost a gold ring, a gold ring, a gold ear pick, two pairs of silver bracelets, one silver dollar, a pearl ear pick, a silver lock pendant, and over 2,000 copper coins. Mao Yucai's family lost seven yuan in legal tender, one silver dollar, 6,000 copper cash, a pair of twisted silk bracelets, two flat bracelets, a gold ring, a gold ring, and a watch. Mao Peisheng's family lost 82 yuan in legal tender, etc. Afterwards, the victims reported the robbery, along with the three iron clubs and the cloth cap left behind by the bandits, to the township head, Guo Yongfen, the district office, and the Public Security Bureau. They jointly went to investigate and reported the incident to the county government, urging a strict investigation and pursuit of the stolen goods.

Kunshan: Police Academy Students Come to Kunshan for Internship 95

Our county is piloting a police district system, which is already taking shape. One hundred and twenty-six students from the Jiangsu Provincial Police Academy refresher course arrived in Kunshan from Zhenjiang on the morning of the 16th for an internship. After one week, they will return to the academy for their graduation ceremony and be assigned to various counties to serve, so as to gain experience. The student dormitory has been set at the Chen Family Shrine on Beitang Street. During the internship, Director Zhang of the Public Security Bureau personally provides guidance. On the 9th of this month, a prisoner named Xu, a smoker, suddenly died in the Fangqiao Detention Center in our county. The result of the examination at the time determined that the death was caused by typhoid fever. Xu Zhen, the son of the deceased, has now learned that his father's death was due to two reasons. After entering the hospital, the opium addiction had not been completely eliminated, and he was sent to the detention center. He had a severe opium craving and asked the detention center for medicine but was beaten instead, causing him to fall to the ground and vomit blood, leading to his death. Another account states that a doctor at the County Hospital mistakenly prescribed medicine, resulting in the injury and death. Given these two versions, a request has been submitted to the county for a re-examination and appeal. Xu Shichang, the judge handling this case, also has many doubts about it and has ordered the warden to file a report.

Implementing Labor Education 96

The preschool primary school in our county is the largest and most developed school in the city, with over one thousand students. The school has as many as two hundred or so delivery workers who bring meals every day. Principal Zou Lianfen, recognizing the opportunity during this period of popularizing literacy, is taking advantage of the opportunity to compile common phrases based on the meal delivery and student pick-up times for these workers. Teachers take turns instructing them for thirty minutes each day, and students at the school review the lessons when they return home. A letter has been sent to the families of each student to discuss and implement this plan.

Wuxi: Eastern Jin Dynasty Ancient City Bricks Discovered 97

In the third district of the county, about three miles from Zhouxin Town, in the Zhangwanli area, which is a necessary route for the Su-Xi Road, there is an earthen mound, about two to three zhang high, and over ten zhang in circumference. Coffins are scattered across the mound and few people visit it. Recently, the Su-Xi Road is under construction and while excavating the earth to fill the roadbed, two large brick tombs were suddenly discovered, buried more than one zhang apart in the middle of the large mound. Each tomb is over two zhang long, six or seven chi wide, and five or six chi high, surrounded by thick walls, and the top is constructed like a city gate arch, using special pointed bricks. Only mud is found in the middle, with nothing else. The ancient bricks of the tomb wall are one chi long, four cun and three fen wide, and one cun and two fen thick. Each brick weighs ten jin, has a dark bluish-green color, and is filled with ancient character; the size is similar to that of city bricks. Another type has diagonal mesh patterns on the surface. According to Cao Hengzhi, an archaeologist in the county, these ancient bricks are called "cloth-pattern bricks" because cloth was used to line the brick blanks during manufacture. One end of the ancient bricks has the seven characters "Fourth Year of Da Xing, August 6th," while the other end has the two characters "One Ten". According to historical records, Da Xing was the reign title of Emperor Yuan of the Eastern Jin Dynasty, corresponding to 321 AD in the Western calendar, meaning that the bricks are 1,615 years old this year. The bricks vary in shape, with the bricks used in the tomb cover being fan-shaped with uneven thickness at both ends and a solid texture. The total number is estimated to be over 10,000, but not all of them have the characters "Fourth Year of Da Xing, August 6th." Although the nearby villagers do not know the history and value of these bricks, driven by curiosity, they are rushing to collect and treasure them.

Quanxing Opium Den Sold Drugs and Was Sealed Up 98

At about 11 PM the night before last, police officers from the Supervisory Office of the Public Security Bureau raided the Quanxing opium den at the Xinglong Bridge embankment in Xiatang within the city and seized five taels of privately manufactured opium. They also found 63 gray drug pills on Zhou Fuxing, a tea room attendant. They further arrested Shi Atong, an opium addict who sold drug pills, at house number 11 on the embankment, and seized an empty iron can that used to contain drug pills. The female cook of the den, Zhang Aren (also known as Zhang Lanying), the manager Ding Renjing, the caretaker Lu Shouqi, the opium paste maker Zhou Baolin, the opium addict Shi Atong, and the general affairs clerk Zhang Amo, totaling six people, were all taken to the bureau. Yesterday (the 16th), they were transferred to the county government, where Military Judge He held a court hearing. As a result, they were ordered to be detained pending transfer to the Commissioner's Office for interrogation. The Public Security Bureau was instructed to dispatch police officers, along with the local Tu Zheng (local head), to seal up the premises of the opium den and conduct further investigation.

Changzhou: Militia Teams Will Be Centrally Trained 99

Hou Houzong, the county magistrate and commander of the militia reserve team, in order to urge all teams to actively conduct training, convened a discussion meeting with the commanders of each company and instructors at the county government on the 15th and decided on the following measures:

The training time is set at 150 hours, starting with military skill lessons.

Centralized training will begin on April 25th at the public sports field.

In addition to the original instructors serving as assistant instructors, the military instructors will have a chief instructor assigned by the brigade headquarters to oversee the training and a horse feed allowance will be provided at the discretion of the company headquarters.

Any militia members who are absent without cause will be punished by the brigade commander and still be compelled to undergo training.

Nantong: Many Opium Offenders, Prisons Full 100

Recently, various counties under the jurisdiction of Nantong district have been continuously sending opium and drug offenders to the Commissioner's Office. After the military judge concludes the trials, they are sent to addiction treatment centers and prisons. The addiction treatment centers, prisons, and opium addict workhouses are all overcrowded. The detention facilities are particularly congested. The Commissioner's Office has specially set up a temporary facility within the office to accommodate them.

Inspection of Nantong Area Water and Land Public Security Forces 101

The Jiangsu Provincial Fourth District water and land public security inspection was held at 8 AM on the 15th outside the West Gate of Nantong, in Xiaoying. Participating police officers included 48 officers and officials and 775 police officers from Nantong, Rugao, Haidou, Taixian, Qidong, Taixing, Jingjiang, and the Third District Water Police. Zhenjiang: Completion of the Dantu Branch River Dredging 102

The Zhenjiang Canal has been in disrepair for years, and residents on both banks arbitrarily dump garbage, causing the riverbed to silt up. During the summer and autumn, boats can still pass, but in winter, the water recedes and the river dries up, making navigation difficult. Even in the spring, the river water rises and falls intermittently, causing inconvenience to navigators. Recognizing that the river is the only waterway for the provincial capital, the Department of Construction ordered the Jiangnan Water Conservancy Engineering Office to quickly dredge it. After receiving the order, the office sent personnel to inspect it. Dredging the Zhenjiang Canal is not difficult, but there are many obstacles, such as removing the houses on both banks. Therefore, they changed their plan to dredge the Dantu Branch River. After the plan was formulated, Gu Houxi was appointed as the director of the engineering office and construction began last December. Since the start of construction, progress has been actively promoted, and the entire project is now largely completed. A stone sluice gate has been built, and the project can be completed by early May. According to news from the Jiangnan Water Conservancy Engineering Office, the completion of the dredging of the canal is of great importance to inland waterway transportation and commerce.

Ningbo: Zhejiang Eastern Salt Collection Begins 103

The four-tenths of the quota of the twenty-fourth year salt amount, that had not been collected from the Zhejiang Eastern Salt 引 (Salt Certificate) Public Warehouse in Yuyao was delayed due to the Pengzhang (Salt Transport Head) objecting to the reform of the official weighing system and the payment of capital. The warehouse official is now in urgent need of sales, so on the morning of the 13th, the Zhejiang Eastern General Office and both the Eastern and Western Sub-Offices began collecting salt at the same time and will directly pay the capital within days. The long-unresolved salt turmoil has thus come to an end.

Local News

Ye Chucang Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning: Visiting Wang Chonghui Again to Discuss the Draft Constitution 104

Dai Jitao and Chen Burei Also Participated; Mr. Ye Returned to Beijing by Train Last Night

According to the Central News Agency, Ye Chucang, the Secretary-General of the Central Party Headquarters and Vice President of the Legislative Yuan, arrived in Shanghai by express train from Beijing at 7 AM yesterday. After getting off at the North Railway Station, he returned to his residence on Avenue Road. Chen Burei, the Deputy Secretary-General of the Central Political Council, visited him at 8 AM. After a half-hour conversation, they went to Mr. Hu's residence on Rue Gounouil to meet Dr. Wang Chonghui, a member of the Central Executive Committee. Dai Chuanxian, President of the Examination Yuan, also arrived later. The four, Wang, Dai, Ye, and Chen, discussed the draft constitution again. They left at 11:30 AM. It is reported that the four exchanged opinions and discussed the points for increasing the transitional clauses in detail, as a reference for drafting the examination report. It is reported that after the Central Standing Committee approves the examination report of the Constitutional Draft Examination Committee next week, it will be sent to the Legislative Yuan to revise the articles so that the draft constitution can be promulgated as scheduled on May 5th. Mr. Ye took the night express train back to Beijing at 11 PM last night. According to Mr. Ye's statement to reporters before his departure, his two trips to Shanghai were both in a private capacity, visiting Mr. Wang Liangchou to discuss the draft constitution. Everything is still awaiting formal approval by the Constitutional Draft Examination Committee (Mr. Ye is the convener of the committee) before being submitted to the Central Standing Committee for approval.

Huang Fu, the former Chairman of the Political Reorganization Committee of the Executive Yuan stationed in Beiping, has been recuperating in Moganshan via Hangzhou since January 17th, for three months now. He then returned to his private residence on Qiqi Road to rest. Because few people knew in advance, no one went to meet him. He came to Shanghai specifically for medical treatment. As for whether he will go to Nanjing, it is currently undecided. Mr. Huang drove out for medical treatment once yesterday morning around 9 AM.

The New Board of Directors of the Public Works Department Held its First Meeting Yesterday 108

Annerly Re-elected as Chairman; Fessenden Appointed as Vice-Chairman

The new board of directors of the Public Works Department of the Public Settlement for 1936-1937 gathered at the Public Works Department Council Chamber at noon yesterday for the first board meeting of this term. The directors present included Mr. Annerly, Mr. Cornwallis, Mr. Fessenden, Mr. Guo Shun, Mr. Xi Yushu, Mr. Xu Xinliu, Mr. Keswick, Mr. MacNaughton, Mr. Mazot, Mr. Brooke, Mr. Bube Tokue, Mr. Yamamoto Takeo, Mr. Yu Qiaqing, and others, totaling thirteen people. The Chinese director Jiang Yiping was absent due to business. Following a motion by Mr. Fessenden and seconded by Mr. Xi Yushu, Mr. Annerly was re-elected as the chairman of the board of directors for this year. Mr. Fessenden was nominated by Mr. Brooke, seconded by Mr. Cornwallis, and was elected as the vice-chairman for this year.

Revision of the Sino-German Commercial Treaty 109

The Silk Industry Association of this City Sends a Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to Offer Opinions

According to the Hua Dong News Agency, merchants in the silk industry in this city believe that in recent years, China's trade with Germany has been declining. The export of 'Fuchou' silk, for example, used to be worth two to three million yuan per year to Germany, but now it only accounts for 10%, which is only 200,000 yuan per year. The situation is extremely bleak. The reason is due to the heavy taxes imposed by Germany. Recently, the German Ambassador, Mr. Knappe, and the economic representatives specially appointed by the syndicate to investigate China's economic conditions and seek progress in Sino-German trade, have been in contact with the Chinese authorities to revise the new Sino-German Commercial Treaty. Before the conclusion of the new Sino-German treaty, three requests are being made, and a letter is sent to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, so that they can be presented for negotiations. The Chamber of Commerce has now telegraphed these three opinions to the two departments for review. The contents are as follows:

Fuchou silk from Henan and Fuchou silk from Andong, Shandong, are made of Chinese wild silkworm silk. They are strong, durable, and inexpensive, and have long been recognized by various countries as the world's most economical materials. Germany should reduce its import tax.

Fuchou silk produced in Henan, Shandong, and Andong is the lowest and crudest grade of Chinese silk. The prices are low, which is different from other Chinese silk goods. It is not a luxury item, but a purely practical commodity. Germany must not classify it as an imported luxury item.

Germany shall not restrict the import quantity of Fuchou silk produced in Henan, Shandong, and Andong that are exported to Germany. It should be given a superior position and an opportunity for smooth sales.

Industry and Commerce Loan Association Continues to Approve Loans 110

Total Approved Amount: 12,050 Yuan

There Are Still Many Who Falsely Report Capital in Hopes of Obtaining Loans

The Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee held its 27th meeting at the China National Goods Bank on Tianjin Road at 4:30 PM on the 15th of this month. The committee members present were Cai Zengji, Qin Runqing, Zhang Peishen, Song Ziliang, Xi Demao (Zhang replacing), Yu Zuoting (Runqing replacing), and Bei Songsun. Chairman Cai Zengji reported on routine affairs, then presented 33 applications for small credit loans. After review, it was decided to reduce the loan amount for some, with the total approved loan amount being 12,050 yuan. Another 12 companies were either declared out of business or their business did not meet the principles for loan approval, and their loan applications were rejected. The applicants will be notified separately of all the approved cases. Furthermore, the committee stated that the applicant factories often do not follow the principles stipulated by the ministry, which is that the amount requested should not exceed half of the capital. Although the committee staff has repeatedly informed them in detail and published notices in newspapers, many still falsely report their capital in hopes of obtaining loans. The committee has decided to directly reject applications that do not comply with the regulations and will not investigate them. Factories wishing to apply for loans should be sure to pay attention and inquire in detail when obtaining the application form at the committee office on the upper floor of the National Goods Bank on Tianjin Road, to avoid being rejected and wasting effort.

The Yili Company Debt Dispute Was Resolved Yesterday 111

Unanimous Support for Four Principles for Resumption of Business

Number of Creditor Representatives Expanded to Seventeen

Shanghai Huashang Yili Soda Company and Yili Glass Factory were forced to close down in September last year and are heavily in debt. The debt dispute could not be resolved, so they sought assistance from the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association. The association convened a meeting of all creditors yesterday afternoon to mediate. With the agreement of the public, four principles were decided and a settlement was announced. Details are as follows:

Representatives Present: The attendees yesterday included 122 creditor representatives, including Cheng Shouchong, Gui Xinyou, Xi Kang, Zhang Hanru, and Chen Baoli, as well as the mediators Yu Qiaqing, Fang Jiaobo, Zhang Jixian, Sun Meitang, Yuan Ludeng, Jin Tingsun, Mao Heyuan, Dong Xingsheng, Zhu Meixian, and Ren Jinping. Yu Qiaqing was elected as the chairman, and Ren Jinping was the recorder.

Chairman's Report: After the ceremony, Chairman Yu Qiaqing reported that the Yili Soda Factory and Glass Factory founded by Xu Tingzuo are famous national goods industries in Shanghai with excellent products. The business was originally very prosperous. However, because Mr. Xu was too enthusiastic about investing in the development of Sanmen Bay, and the financial panic in recent years has become increasingly serious, he was forced to declare bankruptcy last year under economic pressure. The assets of the two factories were taken over by the Hui Zhong Bank, the first priority creditor, and the Meifeng Bank Liquidation Office, the second priority creditor. Mr. Xu believes that the two factories used to have annual profits of 30,000 and 50,000 yuan respectively. If they are sold off at auction, not only will the business be completely destroyed, but the other creditors will inevitably receive nothing. Feeling deeply uneasy, he tried his best to find a way to negotiate with the first and second priority creditors to temporarily suspend the execution. The first priority creditor learned that the two factories do have annual profits and has agreed to temporarily suspend the execution with the consent of the second priority creditor. The first priority creditor is willing to provide additional funds to assist in the resumption of business with the consent of other creditors. To this end, Mr. Xu specifically wrote to the association requesting that it convene all creditors other than the priority creditors to discuss mediation methods. The association believes that Mr. Xu has been very enthusiastic about social welfare and national goods industries in the past. Now that Mr. Xu is facing difficulties, it is appropriate to provide assistance under legal and reasonable conditions. Considering that many of the creditors other than the priority creditors are fellow Ningbo provincials, for the sake of safeguarding the rights and interests of the fellow provincials and other creditors, it is felt that this mediation request is also very beneficial. It is possible to find a suitable guarantee by following this mediation path. Therefore, the association accepted Mr. Xu's request and invited everyone to attend the meeting to discuss a solution, hoping that everyone would uphold the principle of safeguarding their own creditor's rights and safeguarding the national goods industry, and express their opinions. The association is willing to participate in the efforts with everyone's consent.

Principles Resolved: After the report, Fang Jiaobo stated the intentions of the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association to accept mediation. Then, each creditor expressed their opinions. Finally, four principles were decided:

All creditors unanimously support the resumption of business of Yili Soda Company and Yili Glass Factory.

Creditors shall jointly elect representatives to discuss methods for assisting in the resumption of business and repayment of debts.

Based on the above resolution, further negotiate with the first and second creditors to determine a written method for reducing the amount of debt, and request the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association to assist in the process.

According to the second resolution, 17 representatives shall be elected to form a delegation (with creditors holding 5,000 yuan or more as representatives). With the agreement of the creditors, a settlement was announced on the spot, signed by both the creditor and debtor, and will be implemented accordingly.

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, the Sanbei, NingShao, and Lun Shipping Company of this port and the Ningbo Tongyun and GuanCao automobile companies will implement combined water and land transport starting yesterday. Lin Yishun's Coffin Will Be Transported to the Capital Tomorrow Morning 113

Temporary Suspension of Regular Public Funeral at Renxiao Funeral Parlor

According to the Central News Agency, Mr. Lin Yishun, a prominent overseas Chinese leader and pioneer of the revolution, passed away in Shanghai some time ago. It was originally planned that his eldest son, Zhongguo, would escort the coffin back to Singapore for burial on the 14th of this month. However, due to the decision to hold a public funeral, it has been decided that the coffin will be transported to the North Station at 7:55 AM tomorrow and then transported to Beijing by special train. In addition to his son, Zhongguo, those escorting the coffin will include Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee members Zhang Yongfu, Feng Ziyou, Zhang Huadan, Shao Fu, and Lu Shiying, among others. The coffin will be transported from the Universal Funeral Parlor to the North Station without any ceremonial guard of honor. However, the Public Security Bureau band will play music at the North Station to see off the deceased. The special train will arrive in Beijing at 1:50 PM tomorrow. Lin's coffin will be temporarily placed at the Renxiao Funeral Parlor on Mochou Road for burial. His son, Zhongguo, will return to Shanghai in two weeks to await a ship back to the South. Once the burial date is set, he will return to Shanghai and then go to Beijing with his family. A brief biography of Mr. Lin and his contributions to the revolution are attached below.

Mr. Lin's Biography: Mr. Lin's given name is Yishun, and his courtesy name is Fachu. He was from Chenghai, Guangdong. He lost his parents at a young age and lived with his maternal grandparents in Singapore. At the age of ten, he entered St. Joseph's School and graduated at seventeen to study commerce. At the age of twenty, his maternal grandfather passed away, and he inherited a portion of his estate. At the age of twenty-three, he married Ruan Ju'an's eldest daughter, Bixia, and had sons Guo Zhong, Zhong Bang, Zhong Min, and daughter Zhiyu, etc. At the age of twenty-four, he joined his uncle Zhang Yongfu and friend Chen Chunan in engaging in the revolution. Dr. Sun Yat-sen admired his intelligence and entrusted him with handling all matters, large and small. He often engaged in agriculture, planting rubber trees and pineapples. After a year, when the Ba San Wang Company was established, he was appointed as the manager. He then took in comrades who had fled after the Huanghuagang Uprising as assistants, working tirelessly. After three years, he gained assets of hundreds of thousands and became known as the "Pineapple King." The rubber trees also yielded a large harvest, accumulating assets of up to one million. He then built the Zhanhua Villa to entertain comrades who had fled, such as Hu Hanmin, Wang Jingwei, and Bai Wenwei, all of whom were welcomed. After the establishment of the Republic of China, the Provisional President awarded him a Certificate of Honor. Mr. Lin was also extremely enthusiastic about public welfare in Singapore. The British government appointed him as a member of the Agricultural and Forestry Bureau, a Justice of the Peace, and a member of the Opium Review Committee. He was also elected as Chairman or Director of the Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce, the Chaozhou Eight District Association, and the Hua Shang Bank, among others.

Revolutionary Achievements: After the Mao Su newspaper case, Zhang Binglin and Zou Rong were arrested in Shanghai, and Qing officials demanded their extradition. Lin, Zhang Yongfu, and Chen Chunan telegraphed the Shanghai consular body to strongly protest. In the year Gui Mao, Zhang Yongfu and Chen Chunan founded the "Tu Bao" newspaper in Singapore. Lin took on the task of promoting the revolution back in China, carrying thousands of copies of "Tu Cun Bian" (i.e., "Revolutionary Army") and secretly entering Chaozhou, Xiamen, and other places to spread propaganda. In the year Bing Wu, Dr. Sun Yat-sen formed the Tongmenghui (Revolutionary Alliance) in Singapore, and Lin was elected as the director of the social affairs section. Dr. Sun Yat-sen, along with Chen Chunan and Lin, went to Kuala Lumpur to establish the Tongmenghui. They then entered Perak, but were rejected by opponents. They accompanied Dr. Sun Yat-sen into a foreign hotel to avoid trouble. Chen Chunan and Lin were ordered by Dr. Sun Yat-sen to establish the Tongmenghui in Penang and then went with Wu Yingpei to establish the Tongmenghui in Yangon. When the Tongmenghui established the "Zhongxing Daily," Lin was the general manager. During the Huanghuagang Uprising, Lin provided substantial financial assistance. After the failure, many comrades who had fled received assistance from Lin to support their lives. When Yu Jicheng was arrested in Hong Kong, Lin helped to rescue him. After the Zhennanguan Uprising failed, more than six hundred soldiers who fled to Singapore were largely assisted by Lin. When Wang Jingwei plotted to assassinate Prince Regent Zai Feng in Beijing and the matter was exposed, Chen Bijun went to Nanyang to raise funds for his rescue. Lin contributed four hundred dollars. Huang Xing and Hu Hanmin raised funds for the March 29th Uprising in the year Xin Hai, and Lin donated a considerable amount. During the Wuchang Uprising, Lin, Zhang Yongfu, and Chen Chunan formed the Fujian Security Donation and Guangdong Relief Security Donation groups, raising funds to support the military, making great contributions. When Yuan Shikai stole the country, many comrades fled to Nanyang, and Lin entertained them at Honghua Villa, using Tongmei Bank as a secret communications point, which was greatly resented by the local government. During the campaign against Yuan Shikai, Lin provided a lot of financial assistance. When the Guangdong Army returned to Guangdong, Lin once provided ten thousand taels of silver to support the military and raised 300,000 yuan. When Dr. Sun Yat-sen assumed the position of Extraordinary President in Guangdong, Lin personally participated. When Dr. Sun Yat-sen assumed the position of Grand Marshal, he appointed Lin as an advisor to the headquarters.

Long-Term Loans at the End of April: Coordination Between Banks and Money Shops 114

Bank Acceptance Bills Have Achieved Results; Money Shops Set to Discuss Internal Rates on the 25th

With the end of April approaching, banks and money shops have been directly contacting commercial firms and factories that have long-term loans due to negotiate extension procedures. However, loans to commercial firms and factories with poor credit are being recalled. The recovered funds are then being loaned to reliable and well-established commercial firms and factories, making the market very stable. The daily published morning and afternoon Shanghai interbank offered rates (SHIBOR) have been eight fen for several days. However, in previous years, the rates before the end of April were usually between three and four jiao.

Money Shops Scheduled to Discuss Internal Rates: The Money Shops Association will hold a special meeting of member representatives at its offices on Ningbo Road at 1:00 PM on April 25th to discuss internal rates as the end of April approaches. Regarding the 18 million yuan that various money shops borrowed from the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, which has been repeatedly extended, it is said that the money shops that have borrowed the money have received a notice from the Money Shops Supervisory Committee, allowing them to find ways to repay the loans after the end of April.

Acceptance Bills Have Been Quite Effective: Since the establishment of the Bank Union Reserve Committee, which includes bank acceptance facilities, an agreement has been made with member banks whereby member banks can apply to the facility for acceptance of commercial bills. A number of applications have been approved and signed after a thorough review. These bills have been circulating in the market and have been well-received by Chinese and foreign banks and various industries, who are happy to accept them. The facility also publishes the discount rate for 90-day bank acceptance bills daily. Yesterday, it was one jiao and two fen per thousand yuan.

The Total Amount of Negotiable Instruments Has Increased: Since the Central Bank and money shops joined the negotiable instruments clearing house established by the Bank Union Reserve Committee, the total amount of exchanged negotiable instruments has increased. Yesterday, the total amount was 55,598,157.59 yuan, including 14,659,520.10 yuan in exchanged amounts, 37,233,236.68 yuan in transferred amounts, 2,562,101.17 yuan collected on behalf of money shops, and 1,476,205.64 yuan for other items. The overnight lending rate was one jiao per thousand yuan per day.

The Rickshaw Driver Registration Craze Has Generally Abated Yesterday; The Vehicle Committee Continued Registration Yesterday; The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sent a Letter to the Public Works Department to Correct the Quota 117

The Public Works Department's Vehicle Committee accepted the request of the rickshaw owners to continue registering rickshaw drivers, but limited the quota to only 5,000 people. However, there are about 20,000 rickshaw drivers who are unemployed because they have not registered and cannot pull rickshaws. Therefore, they are deeply dissatisfied with this quota. They held a rally and parade on the morning of the 14th, which clashed with the patrolmen, and 23 people were arrested. As of yesterday, the situation has calmed down. The Vehicle Committee has also agreed to continue registration. However, the unemployed rickshaw drivers feel that there is too little porridge for too many monks and that the meager quota of 5,000 is difficult to distribute. Therefore, they are reluctant to come forward. As a result, only a hundred people applied to the Vehicle Committee for registration yesterday.

Chamber of Commerce Official Letter: The Municipal Chamber of Commerce believes that the Public Works Department's Vehicle Committee's continued registration of rickshaw drivers is too small and fails to provide universal relief to unemployed rickshaw drivers. Yesterday, it sent a letter to the Public Works Department requesting correction of the Vehicle Committee's quota and expansion. The original letter stated: "It has been learned that the Vehicle Committee of your department is continuing to register rickshaw drivers based on the request of rickshaw owners. However, there are nearly 10,000 rickshaws in the Public Concession. Owners with two rickshaws are required to recommend one person, and those with three rickshaws are required to recommend one person, limiting the total number to a maximum of 5,000 people. The demand exceeds the supply, resulting in yesterday's conflict between rickshaw drivers and patrolmen. At a time when rural areas are bankrupt and unemployed poor people are flocking to Shanghai, they cannot even find a coolie's life. The Vehicle Committee of your department should take a broader view and handle the matter fairly when continuing to register rickshaw drivers this time. If the restrictions are too narrow, it would be contrary to the Vehicle Committee's stated aim of benefiting rickshaw drivers. It is appropriate to inform your department of the situation and ask you to investigate it. The Vehicle Committee's method of restricting the registration of rickshaw drivers should be corrected quickly to avoid confrontation. We are deeply concerned."

Rickshaw Owners Meeting: The Shanghai Rickshaw Association and the Special Zone Office will hold a meeting of the Custodial Committee at the association at 7:00 PM today to benefit rickshaw drivers and discuss important issues such as raising funds to build dormitories and rickshaw registration. Yesterday, a notice was issued to all committee members stating: "Respectfully, it is hereby ordered that the Custodial Committee will hold a meeting at the association on Lloyd Road at 7:00 PM on April 17th (Friday) to discuss important issues. It is hoped that you will spare some time to attend the meeting on time. Please do not delay. Thank you."

US Asiatic Fleet Commander Moffett Passed Through Shanghai Yesterday En Route to Beijing; Will Return to Shanghai on the 23rd After Transferring to Wuhan 121

Admiral Moffett, commander of the US Asiatic Fleet, came to China from the Philippines, passed through Hong Kong and went to Guangzhou, and visited the Chinese authorities in Southern China. He came north through Fujian and Xiamen, and passed through Shanghai yesterday on his flagship, the Augusta. He did not stop but entered the Yangtze River from Wusongkou to go west to Beijing. After arriving in Beijing, he will transfer to the Isabel and go to Wuhan. He is scheduled to return east and arrive in Shanghai on the 23rd, where he will be stationed.

The French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association Explains the Meaning of Recruiting Members - Reply to the Letter from the Third District Branch of the Municipal Federation 125

Shanghai Times News: The Third District Branch of the French Concession Citizens' Federation sent a letter requesting an explanation because the French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association's recruitment of members was hindered. The Chinese Ratepayers Association replied to the Third District Branch of the Citizens' Federation in accordance with the Association's charter. The original letter stated: "Direct reply: Received your letter, (briefly stating) Recently, our association sent personnel to recruit members within the boundaries of this district. We learned that your association is also recruiting members, which has made our progress quite difficult. However, we believe that your association is the representative body of all Chinese ratepayers in the French Concession. All Chinese ratepayers are members. In short, all Chinese in the French Concession are members. Therefore, there is no organization without members. Now your association suddenly has this act of recruiting members, and our association is deeply puzzled and dares to ask for a detailed explanation, etc." This is approved. Article 6 of Chapter 2 of our association's charter states that any Chinese ratepayer residing in the French Concession who has one of the following qualifications and is registered as a member after issuing an entry card may be a member of this association and have the right to elect representatives to the general assembly: (A) Those who pay donations for properties with a land price of 500 yuan or more; (B) Those who pay more than 10 yuan in house or land donations annually. Therefore, Chinese ratepayers within the concession who have the qualifications for membership but have not registered as members cannot be called members of this association. The association's charter is very detailed. The purpose of our association's recruitment of members is to have the ratepayers within the concession who have not registered as members complete the registration. The above is the reason for the letter and a corresponding reply. I hope you will take note of it. This is addressed to the Third District Branch of the Citizens' Federation, from the Chinese Ratepayers Association."

Tan Jiazhen, Destitute and Down on His Luck, Throws Himself into the Pu River 134

Tan Jiazhen, a native of Huzhou, Zhejiang, is 40 years old and lives at No. 30 Qu Lane, South Gate, Huzhou. He was able to make a living by inheriting his ancestors' legacy, but soon it gradually declined, and he had no skills to develop. Thinking that Shanghai's industry and commerce were the best in the country, he could find a place to settle down and temporarily fill his stomach. At the beginning of this month, he mortgaged all his possessions and set off from Huzhou to find a way, but half a month later, nothing had been achieved, and the funds he carried had been exhausted. Wanting to return to his hometown, he knew it would be difficult to plan. Turning and thinking, he suddenly developed a feeling of厭世, and yesterday afternoon, at the intersection of Pingliang Road and Linping Road, when people were unprepared, he jumped into the Huangpu River. Fortunately, at that time, Patrolman Xi Tan No. 222 led the Yibu and other patrols to pass by the place. Suddenly, they heard the sound of water crashing in the river and rushed to investigate. They were discovered and rescued in a hurry, and sent to the hospital for treatment. Fortunately, he did not drink much water and is expected to survive.
