Wang Yiting Initiates the Construction of a Free Public Cemetery 136

Yesterday, a letter was sent to various charitable organizations for assistance

Wang Yiting, chairman of the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Federation, in view of the fact that the exposed bones of floating coffins in Tongli, Shengze, Lili, Zhenze, Yan, Pingwang, Bei, Hubin, Luxu, Xinta, Beiku, and other remote areas of Wujiang County, Jiangsu, and Jiaxing, Wangdian, Puruan, Wangjiangjing, Pinghu, Xincheng, Huzhou, Tanghui, and other townships in Zhejiang, are extremely tragic, so he entrusted Wang Junsheng, Weng Yinchu, and other directors of the Pushan Villa to be responsible for handling the burial affairs in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The results have been very remarkable in recent years, raising a total of more than 27,000 yuan and collecting more than 80,000 exposed bones. People from all over the world have praised and praised it. A free public cemetery should be held, and preparations are underway. Yesterday, together with Pushan Villa, a letter was sent to the Charitable Organizations Federation, requesting to convene a meeting of various charitable organizations in the city to discuss and provide strong assistance. The letter is as follows: Our villa, since the winter of 1928, has been gratefully assisted by the association with a fund of 2,000 yuan. Director Wang Junsheng personally went to Jiaxing and Wujiang to conduct field investigations. There are more than 10,000 floating coffins along the way. Director Wang worked hard to raise a fund of 27,000 yuan and immediately started work. Up to now, more than 85,000 exposed bones have been collected, with a total expenditure of more than 29,000 yuan. Charity and health have both benefited. Local people have praised and praised it. However, due to the shortage of funds, it is impossible to continue, and the work has been suspended. There are still six or seven thousand floating coffins that have not been buried. The exposed bones are very pitiful and regrettable. Furthermore, the inland atmosphere is bad, and they are often not buried for a long time. This hinders hygiene and obstructs the view. To seek a thorough and complete plan, it is not easy to achieve results if a public cemetery is not held. As for the cemetery land, our villa has 185 mu of Zetian land in the San Gu Temple in Jiaxing, which can be allocated for application. In Wujiang, another 100 mu of land will be found. After its establishment, it will be presented to the government for filing and announced to the public. If there are any more floating coffins, the Baojia chief will be responsible for investigation. If this is done, it will be a permanent solution. It is estimated that it will take 6,000 yuan to start this public cemetery. All coffin burials will be free of charge, so that the bad habits of floating coffins can be corrected. As for the 60,000 unburied exposed remains, other methods should be found to raise funds and buried on the spot as usual. However, our villa is currently experiencing difficulties in terms of funding and has to truthfully submit it. I think your association can advocate in the past and will definitely maintain it in the future. I pray that your association will look at the humble opinions, convene a meeting, and provide strong assistance, so that it can be completed as soon as possible and the merit is immeasurable.

Chen Diaoyuan Gave Gold to Gao Zhiqing, Suddenly a Debt Lawsuit Arose After Gao's Death 138

Friendship is Seen in Life and Death, the Court Approved the Summons of Chen to Court

Chen Diaoyuan, the current President of the Military Senate, and the late Liaoning Gao Zhiqing (Ming Jing) had an old friendship. In 1913, Feng Guozhang served as the Vice President and concurrently as the Governor of Jiangsu. Gao served as Feng's senior adviser, and Chen was the Commander of the Gendarmerie at that time. They were very close and their friendship grew. Later, when Chen became the governor, he appointed Gao as the Secretary-General. Before long, they concluded a marriage between their children. Gao gave his eldest daughter to Chen's second son. Since then,

Increasingly Close. In 1928, they jointly opened the Yucheng Company, specializing in the sale of coal from the Poler Coal Company and the Poler Coal Mine. A contract was signed to exclusively sell the mine's products. At that time, Chen paid 150,000 yuan and Gao paid a capital of 20,000 yuan. Chen was the chairman of the company and Gao was the manager. However, one year later, the debt owed by Poler to Yucheng reached 133,300 gold. Yucheng sued the court for a judgment to repay the amount in installments, including interest, and Chen transferred the debt owed to him.

Gifted to Gao

This was because Chen's second son was unwilling to marry Gao's daughter. At that time, the marriage had already been dissolved. Chen felt deeply sorry for Gao, so in addition to recognizing Gao's eldest daughter as his goddaughter, he also gave him the debt he was entitled to, in order to show his reconciliation. In August of last year, when Gao was critically ill, he wrote a will to distribute the Poler debt to his daughters-in-law Gao Yuxiu, Gao Shengzhenqing, and his grandchildren Gao Zepu, Gao Zehou, etc. Then the heirs jointly submitted a report to the First Special District Local Court

Approved for Management

The inheritance was on file. Now Chen Yinan, who was authorized by Chen Diaoyuan as the legal representative of Yucheng Company, hired Lawyer Dong Yu to file a lawsuit against Gao Yuxiu and other four people in the First Special Court, claiming that after the judgment was finalized, the debt owed by Poler was settled out of court. Poler repaid 145,000 yuan in principal and interest. On the day the settlement contract was signed, 30,000 yuan was paid first, and the remaining amount was paid in installments. Until Gao Zhiqing died,

Poler Collected 30,000

3,000 yuan, not a penny was delivered to the plaintiff, but was deposited in the bank under a pseudonym. When he died, he listed the money he kept that belonged to Yucheng in his will, so that his family could gain illegal benefits. After Gao Zhiqing's death, the defendants secretly collected 6,000 yuan from Poler, so they sued to order the defendants to repay 39,000 yuan in national currency, as well as interest, etc. Gao and others were accused and also hired Lawyer Shi Liang to defend, first stating that Chen Gao had a long-standing friendship and jointly invested in business,

Married for Children

Later, due to disagreements between the children, the marriage was dissolved. Chen then told the story of how he gave all the debt he had obtained to Gao. He then said that the plaintiff was not qualified to sue in the name of Yucheng Company, and Chen Yinan's name as legal representative was also illegal. Finally, he said that Chen Diaoyuan had given the debt to the defendant in the past, and there were various material evidence and witnesses to prove it. Now that his old friend has died,

The Bones Are Not Cold

He suddenly suppressed the facts and argued with the orphans and widows, requesting that Chen Diaoyuan be summoned to the case for detailed trial and to reject the original lawsuit, etc. Yesterday, Judge Zhang Yuhai of the First Special Court opened the court and briefly questioned both lawyers and Chen Yinan. The court approved the defendant's request and ordered a postponement, pending Chen Diaoyuan's summons to court for further questioning.

Chinese Fresh Vegetables: Fiji to Ban Imports 141

Trade with Fiji Plummets

Exports Sharply Decrease

According to a person who engages in procurement and transporting goods to the Philippines, who spoke to this publication, the most frequent exports from our country to the Philippines used to be fresh eggs, lard, raw oil, as well as fresh vegetables and refrigerated cargo. In previous years, just the item of first-grade lard alone could be shipped at least 5,000 tons per month. Now it has decreased to less than 200 tons. As for fresh eggs, in the past, thousands of boxes were shipped at a time, but now they are almost nonexistent. The fundamental reason for this is, first, the Fijian government

increased tariffs

on goods from our country, increasing heavy taxation on Chinese domestic products sent to the Philippines, which adds to the cost. This makes it impossible for Chinese merchants to purchase and sell. Due to the risk of financial loss, Chinese merchants have had to stop trading collectively. Now the Fijian government is encouraging locals to raise chickens themselves. In the future, Chinese fresh eggs will disappear from the island. Other products, such as lard and raw oil, are being

dumped into Fiji by the Japanese

because the Northeast has been lost and the Japanese have gained the production areas. The Japanese are taking advantage of various superior positions to gradually eliminate Chinese goods from the market. The Japanese have already achieved economic and trade priority in various parts of Fiji, and Chinese goods will have even less of a tendency to develop in the future. Furthermore, sweet potatoes, fresh vegetables, and fruits have always been produced exclusively by our country and have been the most profitable exports in our trade with Fiji. However, recently, a reliable report has been received that the Fijian government has already made a decision to ban Chinese

vegetables and fruits

from being imported, and this will be implemented soon. Since Chinese fresh vegetables and fruits will no longer be able to be shipped there, the Fijian government, in order to supply the needs of the people, is already encouraging local cultivation. The major shipping companies in this port, which have an average of twelve to fourteen mail ships sailing to Fiji each month, relied on the above-mentioned lard, raw oil, fresh eggs, vegetables, and fruits as their main exports. Now they are also suffering a major blow, and their business has plummeted. The cargo shipped each time by each ship is less than one-twentieth of what it was a few years ago. This is truly unfortunate.

North Station Joint Transportation Depot: More Smuggled Artificial Silk Seized 142

Two Batches, Totaling Four Large Crates and Eight Large Packages, Valued at Over 3,000 Yuan, All Confiscated

Yesterday, the joint transportation depot at the North Railway Station discovered two batches of smuggled artificial silk being transported from the Tianjin main station to Shanghai. One batch consisted of four large wooden crates, valued at over 1,200 yuan. The other batch consisted of eight large packages, valued at over 2,000 yuan. The total value was over 3,000 yuan. After customs officers stationed at the station reported this to the Inspector General of Customs, at about 2:00 PM that afternoon, the goods were loaded onto trucks and taken to customs for auction and confiscation. It is reported that customs has heard of smuggled goods arriving at the North Station, so they have dispatched several officers to work with railway personnel and stationed them at the station full-time to step up their efforts to maintain customs revenue.

Brawl in the Metropolis Dance Hall: A Tragic Scene 143

Lawyer Chen Passionately in Love with Russian Girl, Old Man Mauko Sues for Injury from Fall

—Defendant Guo Zongwen Did Not Appear Due to Illness—

Lawyer Chen, who resides at No. 31 North Sichuan Road, became acquainted with a 15-year-old Russian girl named Popova. They often went out together, and their friendship was quite deep. They were often seen at dance halls and nightclubs. On the night of September 28th of last year, Chen and his friend, an elderly Russian man named Mauko, went to the Saint George Dance Hall in the French Concession to dance. Suddenly, they saw Popova dancing intimately with a Cantonese man named Guo Zongwen. Chen became enraged. Later, because Guo and the girl went to the Metropolis Dance Hall on Gordon Road to continue dancing, Chen and Mauko also followed them. They chose seats next to Guo Zongwen and glared at him, waiting for an opportunity to act. Around midnight, the two sides began to argue, and then began to fight outside the dance hall. At that time, Chen's companion, the elderly Russian man Mauko, unable to withstand the attack, fled outside. As soon as he reached the entrance, he was tripped by someone, causing his arm to break, and he was seriously injured. However, Guo Zongwen was still unwilling to give up and chased after Mauko, punching him in the back. Eventually, others intervened and persuaded them to stop. The dance hall hired a car to take Mauko to the Baolong Hospital, and the incident was reported to the Xinzha Police Station, which sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. They found Guo at the Saint Anna Dance Hall. At the time, Guo expressed his willingness to pay the medical expenses, and Mauko did not object. So Guo paid 100 yuan for medical expenses, and the matter was settled. Unexpectedly, on the 4th of this month, lawyer Chen Dazhu, representing Mauko, sent a letter to the Legal Department of the Municipal Council, accusing Guo Zongwen of assault and requesting permission to sue. After receiving the letter, the Legal Department reported it to the First Special Court, which issued a subpoena and sent it to the Jing'an Temple Police Station. Chinese Detective Tang Zihong went to Guo Zongwen's residence at Room 211 of the Cangzhou Hotel to summon him. Yesterday morning, Judge Ye Shengchao presided over the trial in the Second Criminal Court. Neither the victim Mauko nor lawyer Chen Daxun appeared in court. The police lawyer Qian Xunjiu presented the above facts and charged Guo with assault under Article 277 of the Criminal Code. The defendant Guo Zongwen did not appear, but sent a lawyer to court, stating that Guo was ill and requesting a postponement. The court ordered that the case be postponed for seven days.

Lu Guisheng Climbs into Sister-in-Law's Bedroom to Rob Gold Lock Piece, etc. 144

Sister-in-Law Awakened and Stabbed with a Sharp Blade

Lu Guisheng, a native of Pudong, used to sell vegetables in the Wuzhou Road vegetable market. Recently, he lost heavily in gambling and was penniless. Unable to raise money, he went to the Zhongshan Hotel at No. 13 X'ian Road late one night. At 4:30 AM, armed with a flashlight and a sharp knife, he sneaked out. From the drying platform of No. 8 Baoyu Lane on Wuzhou Road, where his fellow townsman Gong Chuntao lived, he used a rope to climb into the bedroom of his brother Zhang Xigen's sister-in-law Qiao on the upper floor. He robbed a gold lock piece and a gold chain, worth 300 yuan, which his sister-in-law Qiao had hidden in a drawer. Ms. Qiao was awakened from her sleep and quickly got up to hug him and shout. Lu immediately took out a sharp knife and stabbed her head, face, and back. Ms. Qiao fell to the ground in pain. Lu took the opportunity to abandon the knife and flee. He was apprehended by Chinese Detective Shao Jingfan and Detective Zhang Desheng of the Jiaxing Road Police Station. Lu claimed that he had conspired with Xi Chuntao beforehand, so Xi was also arrested. Both were taken to the police station along with the knife and rope. The injured party was taken to Guangren Hospital for treatment. Yesterday morning, Lu and Xi were brought before the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Municipal Council lawyer Zhang Shizhu explained the case, saying that Zhang Qiao was still in the hospital and requested a postponement. Subsequently, the Chinese and Western detectives reported the details and presented the knife and rope. According to Zhang Xigen, Lu Guisheng was indeed his cousin and at that time, he was selling beef at the small vegetable market. Gong Chuntao was a hired hand and was helping at his stall when the incident occurred. When questioned, Lu Guisheng stated that Xi was an accomplice and was present at the scene with a small knife. When Xi Chuntao was questioned, he denied any conspiracy and requested that the matter be investigated. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered that both be remanded in custody and the case be postponed for further investigation.

Strict Enforcement of Anti-Smoking Campaign Leads to Decrease in Smokers; Six Opium Dens Close Down 145

Most New Licenses for the 25th Year Have Been Renewed; Strict Investigation of Public Officials Protecting Smoking and Gambling Is Absolutely Determined

The new licenses for the 25th year for opium dens approved by the municipal government have already begun to be renewed. Since the strict enforcement of the anti-smoking campaign in Shanghai, the number of smokers has gradually decreased. Therefore, when renewing licenses this year, six opium dens in the northern and southern parts of the city, including Lao Yufeng, have closed down. The Public Security Bureau issued a notice yesterday stating that after finding public officials protecting smokers, they will be severely punished. A reporter from the Dagong News Agency has investigated and reported on the situation as follows:

Opium Den Licenses: Renewal Begins

In the northern and southern districts of the city, opium dens that have been approved to operate by the Municipal Government Public Security Bureau and have been issued business licenses include 12 opium distributors (those who transport opium from Hankou opium warehouses to Shanghai and resell it to opium dens), 54 grade A opium dens, 25 grade B opium dens, and 1 grade C opium den. The business licenses for the 24th year of the Republic have expired, and the new licenses for the 25th year have already begun to be renewed this month. According to news from the Licensing Department of the Public Security Bureau, more than 50 opium dens have already renewed their licenses in recent days. The licenses for a small number of establishments expire between September and October, and they will renew them after they expire.

Six Opium Dens Close Down

Since the Municipal Public Security Bureau began implementing the anti-smoking campaign on July 1st of last year, under the order of the Anti-Smoking Supervision Department of the Military Affairs Commission, more than 35,000 people have registered voluntarily or been forced to register. The number of people sent to smoking cessation hospitals for forced cessation or who voluntarily entered hospitals for cessation has also reached 2,000 to 3,000. More than 300 opium dens have been cracked down on. As a result, the number of smokers in the city has gradually decreased, and the supply of opium has also decreased accordingly. Opium dens with smaller capital have seen sluggish business and found it difficult to maintain operations. Therefore, they inevitably engaged in illegal business and failed to pay license fees and taxes. According to investigations, when renewing new licenses this year, six opium dens, including Sheng Mao Yongchang, Lao Yufeng, Xieji Xingjin, Gonghe, and Zhabei Sanyi Gong, located in the Nine Acres area of the southern part of the city, have all closed down.

Strict Punishment for Protecting Smoking and Gambling

The Municipal Public Security Bureau has recently received confidential reports that a small number of unscrupulous public officials are protecting opium dens, allowing people to smoke, gathering crowds to collect commissions, and profiting from them. Therefore, Director Cai Jingjun of the bureau is particularly resentful of these lawless elements and has ordered all sub-bureaus and district offices to conduct strict investigations and publicize this to all sectors of society. Once discovered, they will be severely punished without leniency.

Zhejiang Provincial Government Approves Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association: Family Graves Exempt from Demolition 150

Strict Investigation of Scoundrels Excavating Graves on Pretexts

The Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai, because the demolition of graves in the Ningbo native cemetery caused disputes, causing panic among fellow villagers abroad, who repeatedly inquired about the situation, almost incessantly. Recently, the Yinxian County government issued a notice stating that all graves in the old urban area must be demolished before May 10, which aroused opposition from fellow villagers. Letters and telegrams were sent one after another, requesting a solution. On the 8th of this month, the Zhejiang Provincial Government was telegraphed to correct the situation. It is now heard that the association received a reply from the Zhejiang Provincial Government on the 1637th of the Civil Affairs Department, approving Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai Yu Hede, etc., a translated telegram, to request Yinxian to correct the deadline for moving actual graves and strictly prohibit excavation. The telegram was approved. It has been found that the relocation of temporary coffins and exposed coffins has been transferred to various counties to eliminate them and allocate land for burial as a result of orders from this government. As for tombs that have been buried for a long time, if they have been registered in accordance with regulations, they can be exempted from relocation. The so-called villages in Yinxian County often have scoundrels excavating graves on pretexts, which should be strictly investigated and dealt with. In addition to ordering the Yinxian County government to report the handling of this case in detail for verification, you should be informed of this approval, etc. The association, fearing that various fellow villagers may not be fully aware of the situation, specifically published the news in the newspaper, stating briefly that graves that have been buried for a long time can be exempted from relocation, and those that have not been registered can quickly register with the township offices in each area to comply with the law, etc. After this clear order is issued, all disputes over the demolition of graves can be temporarily put to rest.

Shanghai's Straw Hat Industry (3)

Chinese Editor

(A Survey of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce, No. 20)

On the straw hat trade: Before 1926, the export of straw hats was entirely controlled by foreign merchants. All foreign export firms in Shanghai engaged in straw hats, with the British firm Anli Xinji, the German firms Lulin and Jiacheng, and the French firm Yongxing being the largest. However, the import and export of goods by foreign firms had to go through the hands of compradores, adding an extra commission and increasing costs and prices. After the establishment of Chinese export firms, because there were no commissions to be deducted, the selling price was cheaper than that of foreign firms. Foreign trading companies were happy to deal directly with Chinese merchants, and the number of foreign firms in Shanghai selling straw hats gradually decreased. Today, only Yongxing and a few others remain. Chinese merchants initially made profits, ranging from over ten thousand yuan for large businesses to seven or eight thousand yuan for smaller ones. After 1931, prices fell, and profits became meager, making business increasingly difficult. In November of that year, the Yuyao Straw Hat Company (located in Shanghai) went bankrupt, with losses reaching 220,000 yuan. The financial community became wary. However, general operations were still stable. Among the firms, Kunhe was the oldest, and Yingfeng was the leader. The organizational structures of the firms are summarized below for reference.

Yingfeng - Established in 1929, it was initially a partnership. The following year, shareholders Yuan Ludeng, Weng Yinchu, and Jin Zhongjian withdrew, and the business was solely operated by the Ma Bole, Ma Shenda, and Ma Shubo brothers. With ample capital, business was quite good and profitable. It also engaged in the export of pig bristles, egg whites, and fur. The address is currently 117 Edward Road.

Kunhe - Established in the early years of the Republic of China, it is the oldest in the industry. It is solely owned by Fu Qilin, with a capital of 140,000 yuan. It has directly engaged in straw hat exports for only the past ten years. It is said that the Ningbo Kunhe Straw Hat Company was established in 1907 during the Guangxu era and is also managed by Mr. Fu. The address is 19 Edward Road.

Ruihe - This firm was transformed from Huasheng, established in February 1935, with a capital of 20,000 yuan. It is a partnership between Wang Shenghe, Shao Jiyun, Sun Zongyou, and Feng Jiming. Feng is the manager and has ties to Lianchang. Transactions with foreign merchants still use the name Huasheng. The address is currently 149 Yuanmingyuan Road.

Lianchang - Established in April 1932, with a capital of 100,000 yuan. Its shareholders are the same as Ruichang, with Li Zuyin also holding shares. The address is currently 149 Yuanmingyuan Road.

Guo Huiji - Established in 1924, with a capital of 20,000 yuan. It is a partnership between Guo Sanjing and Guo Huichuan (deceased). Mr. Guo has branches of Guo Huiji in Ningbo, Haidou, Yuyao, etc., acting as an agent for Yongxing Foreign Company to purchase straw hats. It still exists today. The address is currently 505 Henan Road.

Huitai - Established in 1927, with a capital of 30,000 yuan. It is solely owned by Yang Wenlin. It has branches of Jiatai and Yuantai Straw Hat Companies in Ningbo. The address is 190 Beijing Road.

Huafu - This firm was reorganized on November 1st of last year, with a capital of 50,000 yuan. Former shareholders Zhu Xiangfu and Xu Xiusun remain, and new shareholders Cai Songfu, Zhao Zhaolian, Cai Qinfu, and Xie Junru have joined. Zhu Jincai is the manager. The address is currently 100 Beijing Road.

Hanli - This firm was established nearly ten years ago and is solely owned by the Wu family, with a capital of 100,000 yuan. The address is 467 Jiangxi Road.

Shanghai's straw hat factories date back to the late Guangxu period. Their origin was in Sanguantang, Hongkou. The products were crude, and the raw materials came from Luyi, Henan, hence the name "Luyi straw hats." After 1921, they gradually developed. Small and medium-sized factories were concentrated in the area around Miaoqian Street, Guangqi Road, and Dama Tou. According to a survey in 1931, there were over 90 factories, all small businesses. Some resold their products to larger factories, borrowing their brand names and trademarks to sell their products. After the January 28th Incident, many closed down, including Guanhua, Guanyi, Hualu, Shuangxin, Jiuhua, Wang Hengchang, Yuanchang, Yida, Ming, Lao Dingchang, Qiuji, Yousheng, Shen Hongchang, Shen Taixiang, Li Xieshun, Xie Kang, Jiang Wenhao, Jiang Linji, Huaguo, Huaan, Huasheng, Huaxing, Huatong, Guohua, Zhang Fuxing, Zhang Ruiji, Yixingxiang, Fuji, Yizengfu, Wancheng, Juchangxiang, Gu Tianchang, Guanmei, Huaxiang, and Xinhua. The larger straw hat factories are introduced below, which may give a glimpse of the general situation.

Factory Name Capital (in yuan) Organization Address

Huafu 100,000 Joint Stock Yangshupu Hejian Road

Guanyi 10,000 Partnership 1387 Zhongxing Road, Zhabei

Cao Shiji 8,000 Sole Proprietorship 242 Fangbang Road

Fuji 10,000 Sole Proprietorship 202 Fangbang Road

Fusheng 10,000 Sole Proprietorship 8 Guangqi Road

Huaxing 50,000 Partnership Guangyu Lane, Guangdong Road

Fuli 30,000 Sole Proprietorship End of Yuezhou Road

Fuyuan 10,000 Partnership Tongan Lane, Gongping Road

Xinchang 5,000 Sole Proprietorship 196 Fangbang Road

Hongye 80,000 10 Da'an Lane, Pu'an Jishi Road

Dexing 20,000 Sole Proprietorship Fangbang Road (End)

Educational News

This Year's End, Beginning of Master's Examinations

Conducted by University Graduate Schools

Ministry of Education Stipulates Four Measures Yesterday

(Nanjing, 16th) The Ministry of Education instructed all universities that the Provisional Regulations for the Organization of University Graduate Schools have been promulgated for two years, and the Detailed Rules for the Master's Degree Examination have also been formulated and announced. If any graduate students recruited in 1934 by graduate schools or research institutes established by the Ministry have completed their research period by the end of this year, they may conduct the Master's Degree Examination. The regulations are as follows:

1. Graduate students participating in the Master's Degree Examination must be limited to those whose qualifications have been reported to the Ministry for approval by the graduate school or research institute of the university, in accordance with Article 7 of the Provisional Regulations for the Organization of University Graduate Schools.

2. If the school or institute conducting the Master's Degree Examination has not yet reported the required courses and thesis work of the graduate students to the Ministry for approval in accordance with Article 9 of the Regulations for University Graduate Schools, it should submit a supplementary report for record before the administrative examination.

3. The school or institute conducting the Master's Degree Examination should, in accordance with Article 7 of the Detailed Rules for the Master's Degree Examination, prepare a list of internal and external committee members in advance and submit it to the Ministry for approval.

4. All matters related to the examination should be handled separately by the graduate school or institute of each university and the examination committee in accordance with the various provisions of the Detailed Rules for the Examination. This order is to be complied with.

Extensive Collection, First in East Asia, Continues to Invest Heavily in Purchases

The Science Society Establishes the Shuchu Library Memorial Room for Preservation

Mr. Jin Shuchu of Wuxing is a leading expert in conchology in China. His book, "The Shells of Beidaihe," has been published in two editions and is widely acclaimed, regarded as a standard by scholars. Throughout his life, he spared no expense in collecting scientific books for research and reference. After more than twenty years of continuous collection, he has built the most complete conchology library in East Asia. Some rare volumes were acquired during World War I, and even at a high price today, they would be difficult to purchase. The versions and bindings are meticulously researched, with an emphasis on colored illustrations.

Looking at the illustrations is like seeing the real thing. The collection includes 128 categories with over 2,000 volumes, including over ten complete sets of magazines. All British, German, French, American, Belgian, and Japanese scientific magazines are fully available. Some volumes span decades, making them specialized classics that are difficult to find today. Their value is estimated to be at least 50,000 yuan.

The Biology Institute of the Chinese Science Society is a pioneering private biological research institution in China. Mr. Jin visited Nanjing from Beijing and was impressed by the strong research atmosphere, the hard work of the staff, and the remarkable achievements in recent years. However, due to economic constraints, the institute lacked complete books and magazines. Mr. Jin, as a biologist himself, deeply understood the difficulty of conducting biological research without reference materials. To facilitate scholars' research and to support the development of private research institutions, he discussed the matter with the director of the institute, Mr. Bing Nongshan, and offered to donate his entire collection of conchology books to the library of the Chinese Science Society, for public access to benefit specialized scholars. In addition, he has set aside a fund, using the interest to continue purchasing various related magazines and books. The board of directors of the society unanimously resolved to accept the donation. They expressed their deep gratitude to Mr. Jin for his enthusiasm in promoting scientific research and supporting scientific endeavors. At the end of last month, they sent the head of the library, Mr. Liu Xianjun, to Beijing to arrange for the transportation of the books. It is reported that all the books have been transported from Beijing to Shanghai. The society, to thank Mr. Jin for his generous support, has established the "Shuchu Conchology Library Room" in the Mingfu Library as a memorial. All the books are being cataloged and will be compiled into a special volume, distributed to academic institutions across the country for public access. Mr. Jin's enthusiasm for science and his dedication to public service are commendable.

Lingnan Female Painter, the Xiong Sisters, to Go Abroad for Observation

The Lingnan female painters, the Xiong sisters, Shuangyao, Shuangpei, and Shuang, were invited by President Wang last year to hold an art exhibition in Beijing. Over 20,000 people visited, and contemporary celebrities and scholars praised them highly. It was an unprecedented event in Nanjing's art exhibitions. Subsequently, under the advocacy of Chairman Lin and others, a proposal was made for them to go abroad for observation. It is now known that relatives and friends of the three sisters in the United States and Germany have repeatedly urged them to go. The three sisters have decided to travel at the end of this year and plan to take a thousand paintings with them for exhibition to promote artistic exchanges between young women in Europe, America, and China and to promote Chinese culture. Before going abroad, they plan to hold a pre-departure exhibition in Beijing at the China Road YMCA Auditorium and Reception Hall, scheduled to begin on May 1st. However, this exhibition will only feature four or five hundred works, all recent creations. Works previously exhibited in Beijing will not be exhibited again. The prices of the exhibition works will be reduced to commemorate their departure, with handscrolls and album pages priced at just over 200 yuan each, hanging scrolls priced from one to two hundred yuan, and many priced at one or two tens of yuan. There will also be one or two hundred exquisitely mounted square and rectangular pieces. At the opening, they will create paintings on the spot and give them to guests, charging only four or six yuan to show restraint. Chinese and foreign guests are welcome to request paintings. It is said that the sisters' itinerary will first take them to Germany, then through England and France, and then to America.

Big Win Over Army Team Yesterday

4-0

Jin Shun Scores Three Goals, Shi Jin Also Scores One

(Hong Kong, 16th) The Chinese World Games soccer team played a practice match against the British Navy and Army Combined Team at the South China Stadium at 5:15 PM on the 16th. Further Hearing of Xu Qizhong's Case of Alleged Damage to Creditor Rights 160

After Wu and wealthy merchant Xu Guannan's son, Xu Qizhong, declared bankruptcy, some creditors, including Sincere Company, Sintong Motor Company, Shihe Jewelry Company, Jinjiang Hotel, and a woman named Hu Meiying, believed that Xu Qizhong's bankruptcy was due to extravagance. They hired lawyer Yue Junwei to file a criminal lawsuit with the First Special District Court, based on Articles 154 and 156 of the Bankruptcy Law. The court has already summoned various parties, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Tan continued the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. The plaintiff's lawyer declared that the plaintiffs would all change to managers as their legal representatives and requested correction. They also clearly presented Xu's extravagant accounts one by one. The defendant's lawyer then raised a question, stating that the implementation of the Bankruptcy Law was from October 1, 1935 (24th year), and all the debts owed by the defendant were before the implementation of the law. According to the principle that laws do not have retroactive effect, the case cannot be established. However, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that according to the provisions of the Bankruptcy Law, if there is any act that damages creditor rights within one year before the declaration of bankruptcy, a crime is established. If according to the defendant's lawyer's statement, even if the most recent bankruptcy declarant has an act that damages creditor rights, the law cannot sanction them, which is greatly related to social security. Furthermore, the case of lawyer Liu Fang suing Sun Chunsheng for fraudulent bankruptcy, the facts cited were also acts within one year before the implementation of the Bankruptcy Law. With this precedent, the defendant's defense is difficult to support and requested a postponement in order to present evidence. Judge Tan verified and decided to postpone the hearing for further investigation.

Prostitute Seeks Help, Jumps Out of the Fire Pit 161

Yu Gendi, a 17-year-old woman from Huangdai, Suzhou, was brought to Shanghai by someone a few years ago and sold to Jin Laosan, a madam at the Xiaoyaoge brothel on Dongxinqiao Street in the French Concession, as a prostitute, renamed Hua Ruyu. Every night, when the lights came on, she went out to entertain, engaging in this flesh trade for several years. Recently, Gendi contracted venereal disease. Jin Laosan not only did not allow her to rest and receive medical treatment but forced her to receive guests. If she did not comply, she would be beaten severely. On the 13th of this month, Gendi went to the Oriental Hotel at the request of a guest to stay overnight. She took the opportunity to escape and went to lawyer Chen Chengyin for help. Chen accompanied Gendi to the forensic doctor of the Second Special Court yesterday for an injury examination. At the same time, she filed a criminal lawsuit against Jin Laosan.

Woman Tempts and Kidnaps Girl to Shanghai, Attempting to Sell Her, Apprehended by Detectives 163

Lin Zhou, a woman from Hubei, had been working as a servant in Lei Xianglin's home in her hometown. Unexpectedly, on the 29th of last month, she colluded with her lover, surnamed Lei, to deceive the employer's fourteen-year-old daughter, Xiuying, to Shanghai, hiding her in house number 70, lane 60, Huaji Road, plotting to sell her. Recently, the girl's cousin, Shu Mingqing, found out where she was and reported it to the Hubei Public Security Bureau, which secretly telegraphed the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. Yesterday afternoon, the detective team leader, along with Western and Chinese detectives from the Huishan Police Station, went to the address and arrested Lin Zhou. Together with the Lei girl, they were taken to the police station. The girl was temporarily sent to the Jiliang Institute, and the woman was detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the Bureau of Public Works presented the case and agreed to the transfer from the Municipal Public Security Bureau. According to Shu Mingqing, the Lei girl is his cousin, and Xiuying also confirmed this. When questioned, Lin Zhou admitted that she deceived the girl into coming to Shanghai for fun. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered Lin Zhou and the kidnapped Lei Xiuying to be transferred to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau.

Prosecution for Both Assault and Kidnapping, Wang Yumei's Disappearance Entanglement 164

Wang Yumei, 29 years old, sister of Wang Fufu and Wang Meifu, residents of Yangjing Town, Pudong, is quite beautiful. She used to work in the British-American Tobacco Factory in Pudong. She suddenly disappeared on March 15th. Wang and others searched everywhere, but there was no news. Unexpectedly, at around 2 PM on March 30th, Chen Qiufie, a local employee of the factory, along with a woman named Meizhen, went to Wang's house to inquire. Wang's friend Luo Bingrong happened to arrive at Wang's house to report a secret, claiming that Yumei had been lured away by Chen and his daughter. Thus, Wang Fufu, Wang Meifu, and Luo Bingrong chased Chen Qiufie to a rice field, where they surrounded and beat him, causing injury. The noise attracted the police, who brought them all to the police station and transferred them to the local court. After investigation by Prosecutor Xiao, Wang Fufu, Wang Meifu, and Luo Bingrong were released on bail and prosecuted for assault. Chen Qiufie and Chen Meizhen were detained and prosecuted for kidnapping. At the same time, Wang Yumei suddenly appeared and returned home. However, when the case was heard yesterday in the Criminal Court by Judge Chen Kangsun, Chen Qiufie and his daughter hired lawyers Zhan Jifeng and Zhan Yiwang to defend them. Wang Yumei testified in court, saying that her going out was at the invitation of other young women to go out and play, and she stayed at the young women's place, which had nothing to do with Chen Qiufie and his daughter. After this testimony, the judge immediately declared the debate over. The defendants Chen Qiufie and his daughter were released on bail to lawyer Zhan. The case is adjourned for a combined judgment.

June Makes Its Debut: Gold Market Still Struggles to Rally

Supply and Demand Disparity Creates a Vague Trend, Down Two Yuan Even with Swap Calculation

The June gold market debuted yesterday, still struggling to rally. The overall trend remained peaceful, though it appeared vague at times. Factoring in the control period, it still fell slightly below two yuan. The trend seemed stable. In the early morning, overseas silver markets saw London rise and America remain flat. Large trading firms claimed the market would stabilize after closing. A few Indian firms placed orders to buy at the listed price. Upon entry, the near term remained stable, but the long-term trend was weak, reportedly due to more sellers. The long-term silver price in Delhi did not move but rose by four li. The exchange rate remained flat. The London gold price did not move; the central bank announced its listed price, with both England and America flat. Customs gold units did not move. The standard gold bar price remained at 145.2 yuan. Over-the-counter forward trading opened at around 43 yuan. Factoring in swap calculations, it still paled in comparison. Dadecheng took advantage of the high prices to sell bars, resulting in slight delays. After opening, demand and supply among large firms diverged, but prices remained stable. Shen Bao Literary Weekly

Wen Xiaoyu 197

— Long Gonggong

Since that young unemployed blacksmith came to live here, Wen Xiaoyu has become a timid and shy girl. Her face is as white as paper, covered with many small red pimples. Her large bones tremble unnaturally, her voice is as low and tight as a sheep, and she often sighs without saying a word. When our landlords, who live by lending money, invited us to dinner, this young lady couldn't eat anything and even broke a spoon.

When she passes our door, her steps become more solemn. Sometimes she deliberately drops something, then picks it up with a red face, acting flustered... This proud middle school student used to only show me a face as stiff as a stone slab.

One Sunday morning, a week after the young blacksmith left, the weather was warm, the bone-chilling north wind had stopped, and the yellow clouds were leisurely sinking and floating in the sky. Wen Xiaoyu burst into my room, her posture as if someone had bumped into her hard from behind... she practically jumped in.

"Do you know what kind of guy the little blacksmith is?... Alas, you don't know..." she said excitedly, her eyes darting around nervously. "He actually expressed his love to me!"

"Really?"

"Yes, really. Although we live in the same house," she paused as if recalling something, then continued, "he often writes letters to me. We haven't really talked seriously. But a blacksmith writing letters—doing something so clever and capable—is quite rare!"

My surprise dissipated. I knew the young man had written her many letters, but there wasn't a single sentence about love in them. I asked her to sit down, poured her a cup of tea, and faced the mirror—which was a piece of glass in the window frame, with newspaper pasted on the back—to pluck my own beard.

"Did you promise to correspond with him?" I asked.

"Promise?—I didn't say anything. But... yes, that's how it is... he often hands me letters."

"Is he showing off his literary talent?"

"No! Look, he writes me letters about marital matters!" Wen Xiaoyu said with obvious seriousness. "I know what this young man is up to—a very simple intention."

"Are there things he wrote that you admire? This child is treated unfairly by society, but he wants to show his talents at every opportunity," I said clearly.

"I pity him," she admitted.

"Sometimes I feel that his life is very interesting, while mine is plain and tasteless. He seems to know everything, this melancholy young man, and he has a very good literary talent. —It's hard to find one or two like him in school!"

Before I could answer, she spoke again, confused and hysterically.

"In any case, he shouldn't have such thoughts so early on. He should admit that it's his fantasy. Even so, he's too fast!... Someone like that, no one would approve of me even saying a word to him... You know his character, he's very proud: I even told him, I said, 'You always mix in those colloquialisms, if you were a student, you'd know how the graders would scold you!'"... Yes, he is really prejudiced and stubborn, not like a young man..."

I asked her, "Why are you telling me all this?"

"You tell him, tell him everything—"

She said it unintentionally and stopped abruptly. At first, she had stumbled into my room unintentionally—that's how she made me feel, and now she felt strange. She looked around restlessly at our beds, the corner of the wall piled with washbasins, mouthwash cups, and shoeboxes, and other places. She had never walked into our room alone before.

"Perhaps, this is not very good," she said after a while, correcting herself. "There's no other meaning in me talking to you... Whatever we've said, don't say a word to him."

April 14, 1936.

Spring Outing 198

— Jiang Jing

The decision to go to Longhua was made the day before the spring break, so it was very rushed. The process of deciding was actually quite funny. If the male teacher hadn't wanted to take the opportunity to play with the female teacher, they wouldn't have thought about the children in particular. Unfortunately, the female teacher didn't go after all. This clearly affected the short trip.

Of course, the children didn't understand any of this. When the teachers announced in their classrooms that they were going to Longhua for a trip, everyone cheered happily. It's so annoying to have class and dismissal every day! "I'm going!" "I'm going!" The shouts came from everyone's mouths.

The children in the city are really too stifled by the shops and smoke, especially these children from poor families. They can't see nature except for the sky, and even the earth has been covered up, so when they arrive in this semi-rural suburb, they find everything new and strange. Whoever sees a willow tree first shouts eagerly, "Willow! Willow!" Whoever sees a paper kite first shouts the name of the paper kite, or a butterfly, or a centipede, and the other children follow suit, shouting as if competing to see who can shout the loudest.

We arrived at the intersection of Dapu Road and Xukou Road. Originally, we should have turned right onto Kangxou Road, but the children insisted on walking along the railway in front. "There's a bridge on the railway, it'll make you dizzy!" I warned them.

"No, it won't!"

"Hmm! If you're not careful, you'll fall into the river!"

"No, it won't!"

This time, no matter what I said, it didn't work, they always retorted with "No, it won't," "No, it won't." What could I do? In fact, although the walkway on the railway wasn't as wide as the road, there wasn't any coal cinder rising up with your feet. When you step down, one step is one step. The children naturally didn't care about all this, they deliberately stepped on the stones beside the sleepers and crossed back and forth on the railway. They did such silly things with great pleasure.

The memorial tower for the fallen soldiers of the Fifth Division of the Army stood in front of us. An older child said seriously to his companions:

"Bow! Hey, bow! It's to commemorate the 'January 28th' incident!" He took off his hat and bowed three times, and several others followed his example.

Now, we stepped onto the streets of Longhua. The houses on both sides of the road were still houses, just like in Shanghai, but they weren't as grand as the houses in Shanghai. "Is this Longhua?" The children simply couldn't believe that this was the place they had been looking forward to.

Fortunately, Longhua wasn't just like that. The leading teacher first took us to the temple. There were so many people inside. And so many Buddhas. But there was even more smoke from incense and paper, filling every hall. In some halls, it even smoked your tears out, making it impossible to bear.

In front of the temple was the Pagoda of Gratitude. It was open at this time, allowing people to climb it. This became a place of joy for the children. They insisted on going up. According to the rules, each person had to pay ten cents to go up. But we received preferential treatment and only spent twenty cents in total. When we stepped onto the stairs inside the pagoda, I felt a kind of terrifying responsibility, "What if the pagoda collapses...?" Although we all came out safely, I always felt that I had taken them on a dangerous adventure.

Appreciating Camellias 199

— Yuan Jian

The children originally wanted to see peach blossoms, but when they asked others, they didn't know where there were any. Now, we only had the airport to see.

After eating! Actually, we ate light noodles for five cents a bowl! Afterwards, because it was still a bit of a walk to the airport, we first rested in a park to the left of the temple. There was also a memorial tower for fallen soldiers here, but the children didn't bow. To prevent the children from being thirsty, the teachers distributed some sugar cane to each of them. Because some of the children weren't full, they also gave each of them two beef buns. The impatient children had already bought willow branches and peach blossoms at this time.

As soon as we entered the airport gate, we heard a buzzing sound. A plane was preparing to take off. This was really good luck for the children. They shouted happily "Oh——, let's go see!" and then ran away, leaving us far behind. One of the older girls, focusing only on watching, didn't pay attention to her feet and tripped in a ditch beside the road, causing the workers who were mowing the grass in the field to laugh until we passed by.

The plane flew out of sight. But there were other planes being repaired in the field. The children surrounded them again. At this time, one of the children touched the wing of the plane and was shouted at by a worker, and the child looked very embarrassed.

Since the wings of the plane were not good to touch, their attention turned to the vast grass field. How vast. How green. How good for somersaults. They were tempted by it. Like a swarm of bees, they rushed straight to the center of the grass field. Unfortunately, they had only run a few steps when they were forbidden by the guards. They had no choice but to stare blankly at the grass.

Alas! What can we do to satisfy these children's hard-to-satisfy hearts?

The First Tears of Disappointment 200

— Zang Kejia

"The Central Government is recruiting for the Navy."

After the Dean of Students announced this news he had brought from Jinan in public, the area in front of the office was crowded with people. Everyone mumbled something, smiles on their lips, as if a bright shortcut had opened up before everyone.

"Go away, go away, those who are tall, don't come!"

These words were like a gust of merciless wind blowing away the tide in front. The older ones needless to say walked away with disappointment, the ones who were about the right age but a bit taller complained that they shouldn't have grown so tall!

"Teacher, see if I can do it?"

Some children who thought they had a bit of hope, looked up, waiting for the Dean of Students' answer. Smiles and hand-waving replaced the answer. But they all clung on stubbornly, unwilling to leave, as if the land in front of the office door could be used to plant their hopes.

"If your height doesn't meet the requirements, it's a waste of travel expenses, you don't listen when I tell you!"

The Dean of Students spoke and picked up the cloth ruler in his hand. This ruler was merciless, if you stood in front of it, it could dismiss you without saying a word. The ones who were a bit too tall slightly bent their bodies, imitating inchworms, not daring to lift their heads under the black surface of the cloth ruler.

The cloth ruler was stern, many people failed its permission and walked away disappointed.

Opening eyelids to check for trachoma, showing arms to check skin, the Dean of Students was like a doctor concerned about the health of his students.

Checking and checking, only seven grains of gold were found in a pile of sand.

These seven lucky ones were from different classes, but they were all about the same age and build, if they stood together to compare, they would at most be no more than a head or an ear root apart.

They were enthusiastically busy collecting travel expenses, busy borrowing bicycles, to save money, they decided not to take the bus, not to take the train. On the morning of the day they left, the seven people lined up and walked out of the gate, clusters of classmates watched them go, turning back and disliking their books even more, feeling that their own future was even more uncertain. Picking up a broken lecture note, they hummed in a bitter, dry tone:

"Old nests are suitable for mud-carrying swallows,

Flying to the branches to become phoenixes!"

This small line of seven left the school gate, six people stepped on their bicycles, the smallest one, Linsheng (the most adorable child), clung to the back of someone else's bike as a tail, this day a yellow wind raged, dust like rain, pushing the wheels of hope towards the unfamiliar road a hundred miles away. These seven children were all leaving their hometown for the first time, Linsheng repeatedly asked the Dean of Students before leaving:

"Please, teacher, write a letter and tell my mother."

The students' envy for them had not yet faded, but this line of seven was suddenly blown back by the sky-filling yellow wind. Hearing this news, I rushed to the dormitory to ask them, only to find out that Linsheng was the only one who qualified in height, and he had also returned because he was afraid of being alone. Seeing them all covered in dust, sitting on the edge of the bed like a stone. The older ones had a bigger heart, and after murmuring, they still boasted to their classmates about the scenery of Jinan, and I also comforted them with the words "a blessing in disguise." Finally, I went to Linsheng's room, it was cold and quiet with only him hugging a thick quilt and sleeping, I woke him up and saw tears in his eyes. I used all sorts of words to warm his little heart, but his tears brushed my words off his face.

Mother Wang and the Doctor 202

— Yang Sao

Hey, esteemed readers, hey,

This is a true story;

You can believe it as you read on,

But I don't know if it will become poetry.

"You need to breathe some fresh air, take some tonic medicine, Vitamin A or chicken essence..."

"Sir, I can only live in the kitchen lean-to,

I can only eat congee, pickled mustard greens, preferably dried fish."

"That won't work," he washed his hands with soap,

"The disease has already entered the second stage, without treatment, you'll only die!"

"But sir, what can I do? I only earn five dollars a month, and I have a little daughter..."

"What does your husband do?" He dried his hands and put away his stethoscope.

"A'Jin's father works in the countryside; we ran away because life in the countryside was hard."

"Ahem, then I don't know! I only know what kind of treatment your illness requires..."

"Then, sir, please treat me..." The hope shone in her feverish face.

"Yes, yes!" He sat down and wrote a prescription, gently placing it in Mother Wang's dry hand.

"What kind of medicine is this, is it expensive?" Her trembling hand nervously pressed her wheezing lungs.

"This is, this is a bottle of Vitamin A, a fair price, seven and a half dollars, the medicine is very effective..."

"Oh!" She was even more surprised than hearing about death, constantly coughing from her decaying lungs.

"Okay, okay, I'm very busy, what about my consultation fee? Including the transportation fee, let's count it as ten dollars, a cheap price..."

"Oh!" Her heartbeat almost stopped,

Pressing her wheezing, her two frightening eyes bulging.

"Alright," he picked up his black leather bag and wanted to leave,

"What about my consultation fee?" He stretched out one hand longingly...

Hey, esteemed readers, hey,

I don't know when the doctor's hand retracted.

This story probably won't become poetry, I don't know how to end it!

Reflections Among the Peculiar Rocks 203

— Yu

Although the time seemed like a fleeting moment, the impression was very profound. I climbed to the summit of Tianping Mountain through the narrow, winding path between towering rocks. The mountain wind blew from behind, clouds descended from above, and rain lightly dotted my face from the side. I wanted to take a breath of free air, but the anxiety in my heart prevented me from such leisure. There were a total of four people, one of whom retreated halfway. Only three of us managed to reach the summit, and each of us wore a serious expression, carrying the same heavy mood. I couldn't discern their inner emotions from their faces, just as they couldn't understand mine. I vigorously raised the lapel of my overcoat, looking at the undulating mountains around us, which formed an oval-shaped valley. Pine trees followed the slope of the mountain, creating rows of varying heights. The branches of the pine trees swayed in the wind, seemingly welcoming our group. Their surging roars also seemed to intimidate us, as if they sensed the heavy urban air about us, knowing we were not those who lived within their embrace or resided on their fringes. We were strangers to the mountains, naturally not expecting any creatures to welcome us, nor fearing any to threaten us. They understood our mood. We advanced along the dark path, interspersed with sand that made it easy to slip. We didn't hear the chirping of spring birds, nor did any crows take flight because of our passing. Only a few hungry eagles in the distance, flying almost as high as the summit, emitted shrill and resounding cries that struck into our hearts. Their cries were certainly not meant for us. They were indifferent to us. We had such a feeling, but perhaps they didn't even have that feeling. Thus, we sensed their existence, but they circled alone and fiercely, focusing their attention on the task of finding food, without noticing our presence.

I admire eagles for their courage, yet I detest them for their greed and exclusivity. Although our great poets have defended them, "The wild bird does not flock; it has been so since ancient times." Although the Italian patriot and liberal Mazzini, in his famous essay "Goethe and Byron," said that Goethe and Byron were like hungry eagles hovering in the skies of the early 19th century, their shrill and disappointed cries shook the hearts of people on the European continent at that time (the gist of it, as I don't have the book at hand to verify). But the characteristic of our era is no longer personal inner turmoil, but the painful lives of the masses. The watershed between the past and the present seems to lie here. As representatives of the literary characteristics of the early 19th century, "Faust" and "Manfred," we can learn from Goethe's words about Byron: "This outstanding and talented poet (referring to Byron) will transform my Faust into himself, and extract from it an extremely strong nourishment for his melancholy taste. He has his own individual methods, his own purposes, using the power of inner impulse, so all those are not original, and especially because of this reason, I cannot but admire his genius." It can be seen that these two masterpieces have the characteristics of their common era. But I still don't understand Faust well. I don't understand German. I have read Guo Moruo's Chinese translation of Faust, Part One, and the English translation of the entire Faust, but I was not moved by them. On the contrary, Byron's Manfred, when I was still a simple and naive child escaping from that bloody world, closed myself in a small attic, and when I opened this poetic drama to read it, it gave my heart a tremendous impact. Especially when Manfred was dying, rejecting the sermon of the priest who wore the clothes of the dead, it aroused a reaction in the depths of my heart.

You have no power over me, I feel that,

And you will never govern me, I also know,

What I have already accomplished is done; I conceal within my heart

A trauma, nothing will be gained from you;

The eternal heart itself

Takes revenge for its good thoughts or evil thoughts—

It is its own beginning of sin and also the end of sin—

And its own emptiness and time—its inherent sensations when freed from this impermanence—

Gains no color from the transient external things;

But concentrates on pain or happiness

And these are born of knowledge from a barren heart.

You have not tempted me, nor can you tempt me;

I am not your puppet, nor your prisoner—

But in the past, I was my own destroyer, and I will

Always be my own destroyer. —Withdraw, you deceiving devil,

The hand of death is approaching me—but not yours!

If Manfred is the incarnation of Byron, then Byron, in my eyes, is respectable for his spirit of resistance, his unyielding character. The most annoying thing in the world is those vulgar and tedious preachers in black robes. They use deceptive means to try to exchange your conscience, to try to shift your goals, to try to use numbing drugs to temporarily relieve the pain caused by the disharmony between you and the objective environment. They deprive you of many things, but they never give you anything in return. In short, in order to maintain the dignity of the decayed puppet dug out of the earth and the sinful shrine placed inside the puppet, they will use any means. If you have self-awareness, a sharp eye to see through all this, and if you still have a bit of primitive courage, or the ambition to destroy this decaying puppet at will, you will see the priest in black robes, his eyes red, his mouth twisted, and hot steam spraying from his pores. He will present to you, one by one, the dogmas or moral laws left over from a certain tribal society, and tell you: According to a certain dogma or moral law, you should be punished; according to a certain dogma or moral law, you should go to hell; according to a certain dogma or moral law, you should lose your soul. If such dogmas or moral laws cannot convince you, then he will use the name of the puppet to say that you are a heretic, a believer of Satan, because you have two bright eyes, your eyes must be gouged out; you have two active hands, your hands must be cut off; you have a fairer conscience, your heart must be cut open; you have a tongue to convey your thoughts, your tongue must be pulled out. He even thinks that you have reached a considerable age and you don't have much ability to move around, you may grow a smarter and more excellent second generation who will inherit your thoughts and actions. So the most barbaric and fundamental method appears: they will eliminate your ability to reproduce. This method, which has existed in ancient China, is seen in the laws of a certain society represented by certain people in modern times who use science as a talisman.

Such sermons from black-robed priests, such barbaric remnants, are still the same in the early 20th century as in the early 19th century. We have not seen much change in the qualitative aspect, but only that its fog is even thicker. Although an explosive primer has long been buried on the social foundation of a group of deceivers, it seems that we still need to wait in time for this primer to produce bright and colorful sparks. However, what is pitiable are those Pgukustubes who have absorbed the toxic substance of the times. They think that it is right to use other people's flesh and blood to nourish those black-robed priests, and to get some leftovers from it. They advocate aggression, advocate slaughter, and as a result, the people of the world suffer from their poison, and they themselves and their descendants also suffer such a fate. The similarities between 1936 and 1914 are many. And what is most pitiable is naturally not those who have died, but we who are still alive. We who are still alive are too shameless, too unbrave, and too unconscionable. The poet Ralph Chaplin, who was imprisoned in Leavenworth Prison during the Great War for opposing war, wrote a poem "Mourn Not the Dead" which is enough to shame us cowards:

Mourn not those who lie on the cold ground,

Corpse next to corpse—

The silent and compassionate earth caresses all the dead

As all men must be;

Mourn not your captured companions, you must be detained

Too firmly to break free—

Each in an iron coffin,

Buried alive there;

Rather mourn those merciless mobs—

The timid and gentle people

They see the extreme misfortune and error of the world

Without speaking out.

We should have such courage to point out all the evils in the world. But what is the reality? If we look back and examine ourselves, we are all obliterating the truth and acting as the most shameless and base liars in the world. This has its objective reasons. To eradicate this reason, we must gather strength, which cannot be done by the strength of a brave giant (Titan) as expressed in the literature of the 15th century; nor can we fulfill our task by expressing personal inner distress deeply in literature. We must have great courage and advance towards a common goal. There are objective reasons for creating universal hypocrisy. What exactly are these objective reasons? Naturally, it cannot be fully explained in a few words. One day I heard a story. Although the content of this story is very superficial, its meaning is quite profound. The plot of the story is roughly like this: A wealthy man used a large bonus to reward a lie that had the greatest impact on society. As a result, three people all claimed to be entitled to this bonus. The first was the creator of the lie that had the greatest impact. Because he created the lie, the award should be given to him. The second was the spreader of the lie. Without him, the lie would not have had an impact, so the award should be given to him. This was also quite reasonable. The third was the preserver of the lie. Without him, the lie would not have been spread, so the award should be given to him, which was even more justifiable. Each of these people claimed the bonus and refused to give in, so the wealthy man had no choice but to consult a wise judge. The judge's judgment was beyond the expectations of these three people. The judge believed that none of them were qualified to receive the award, and that the award should be given to a fourth, forgotten man—society. This judge understood the truth quite well, and his judgment was also brilliant.

Therefore, if we attribute all the misfortunes created by the present society to individuals, to the specific greed of a group of people, or to human sin, to the impulses of individuals' hearts, we are distorting the facts and shifting humanity's goal towards the light. Spiritualist philosophers start from the heart, abandoning objective reality, and turn to the individual's heart in order to achieve peace and order in the world. I ultimately believe it is the fantasy of a sick person. For decades, Chinese history has been following a cyclical path, I am afraid it is caused by these vulgar philosophies. But there are still people taking hoes, shovels, and stone rollers to do repair work on this road, and as a result, I think their repair project will definitely be buried in the weeds, and the people doing the repairs will also die in the weeds. On the other hand, people who are unwilling to die in the weeds will naturally, based on their faces of not being willing to be slaves, stretch out their hard bodies that are unwilling to fill the graves of the cowardly, draw out the sword of fighting for freedom, and emit eagle-like cries, facing head-on the enemies who invade us, slaughter us, and plunder everything from us. The enemies are the supporters of this deformed society and share the remnants of the loot created by this deformed society.

Ways to Relieve the Spring Famine 204

— Xiaoshan

"Central News Agency, Xi'an Dispatch" The spring famine in southern Shaanxi is severe. In remote areas, tree bark and grass roots have become the main food. The Provincial Relief Committee is raising funds for relief efforts and plans to raise 70,000 yuan to carry out relief.

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Military Commission yesterday instructed the Hubei Provincial Government, saying: "According to reports, the famine in Yichang is severe, and there have been incidents of starving people seizing food. Please instruct to quickly provide relief to maintain order." In addition to instructions, please quickly devise effective relief measures and report them for verification...

People living in the fertile lands of Jiangnan seem unaware of the spring famine, just as they were unaware of the drought and flood disasters in the northwest years ago. There, tens of millions of disaster victims died miserably, and those in Jiangnan seemed unaffected. In Shanghai, we have never even dreamed of the tragedy of the spring famine.

Now, the spring famine in the southern Shaanxi area and the spring famine in more than 20 counties in Hubei Province have appeared again in a year of chaos. From the news in the newspapers, we can see that the masses in southern Shaanxi have tree bark and grass roots as their main food. If it is delayed any longer, we believe they will not even have wet clods of mud to eat. The same is true in Yichang, Hubei, where people are seizing food. For the sake of survival, order has been disrupted. The entire province of Hubei is also in a crisis of wind and rain. We will not forget that after the floods in the Xianghan Yangtze River last year, many counties in Hubei Province suffered autumn famines. At that time, there was no way to provide relief, and this year's spring famine will inevitably be ten times more severe.

However, this famine is not limited to the poorer provinces of Hubei and Shaanxi. The economic bankruptcy of many other provinces has not been a matter of a day or two, but a long-term and widespread phenomenon. Our authorities have indeed had many disaster relief efforts, but those are only superficial relief, not fundamental relief. We have seen from the past to the present that disasters and banditry are the same everywhere. The lives of the people have long been unable to struggle. Every disaster results in death or escape. Where to escape to? In the end, it is death, because everywhere is under economic bankruptcy. It is not enough to think of relief measures temporarily. On the contrary, it is completely useless.

Judging from the news, southern Shaanxi has reached a dead end, and the Provincial Relief Committee is only "planning relief measures and plans to raise 70,000 yuan to carry out relief." I think the Relief Committee should have tried to provide relief earlier. Now that they are only thinking about it, I am afraid that many people have already died.

In Hubei, the fact that people have fought each other for food can also prove that we do not try to prevent disasters in advance, and after disasters, we cannot thoroughly and practically provide relief. It is only after a long time that we decide on the old tricks of the past: "In addition to making every effort to raise relief funds and distribute them, we will also telegraph the central government to allocate spring relief and increase the distribution of charitable relief. We still hope that the authorities will provide fundamental relief measures to eliminate the crisis in its infancy and maintain the lives of the people..." We understand that that set of measures has been the same for many years, and relief is called relief, but famines continue to occur and are getting worse day by day. We are still waiting for the so-called fundamental solution until we die, but we don't know when it will appear!

Drunk 205

"Go... I'm not going; I'm sleeping here with you... little sister-in-law..." He muttered vaguely.

The shop assistants laughed again.

"What are you laughing at..." Saying that, she also giggled. She knew that he would do this when he was drunk, so she shouted at him loudly: "Hurry back, your wife ran away with a monk, you living turtle..." The female shopkeeper couldn't stop laughing, she shook her waist and couldn't catch her breath from laughing.

The man was like a madman, his terrible eyes filled with bloodshot, he slammed a fist heavily on the table, the things on the table jumped, and he pulled out a sharp knife from his arms. The knife "clicked" as he stuck it into the table, and he began to cry.

The female shopkeeper was stunned.

"Go back, let them send you back, shall I call a car..." The female shopkeeper was afraid that he would cause trouble, so she said softly to him, her tone seemed to be begging him.

"No, I'm not going back..." he said crying, like a naughty child. The shop assistants were happy to see the excitement and were about to laugh again, he glared at them fiercely. "...I'm not going back... I'll be angry when I go back... I'll be jealous, I can't wait to kill those bastards who occupy my wife... You don't know: you don't know: Ah! My wife is a..."
